date: 2016-12-27
to: Clem Hobson <clem@beeline.co>
subject: Re: Catching up before Chrimbo
msg_id: 159422890ed3c3de
---

Hey Clem,

I looked into this a little bit more deeply. Here's the documentation I've
been referring to:

   - http://www.jonloomer.com/2014/04/14/facebook-conversion-
   tracking-google-analytics/
   - http://www.smartly.io/blog/facebook-vs-google-analytics-
   deep-dive-into-conversion-tracking-and-attribution-models
   <http://www.smartly.io/blog/facebook-vs-google-analytics-deep-dive-into-conversion-tracking-and-attribution-models>
   - https://support.google.com/analytics/answer/1662518?hl=en

There are some things we could tweak on both the Facebook and the GA end to
make these stats more similar. However, it seems that some Facebook sales
will never properly track to Google Analytics (there are certain visitor
types apparently that GA can't see - some sort of webframe layer that
Facebook uses for ads sometimes).

There's also the fact that Google Analytics uses last-click attribution. If
you'd like, we could make a custom attribution model? Sounds like a fun
project to me. But still likely won't capture some of this data in GA -
keep in mind Facebook has a strong incentive to attribute every purchase
they are vaguely responsible for - GA is a free tool that's most easily
integrated with AdWords and attributing value to search PPC, so slightly
misaligned incentives from a platform standpoint - I would trust Facebook,
but take it with a grain of salt that that might just be 1 of the 3
necessary impressions to facilitate a conversion. As it is now, GA will
show the source that spurred the last touchpoint to conversion, which is
generally the most valuable.

All to say, we can get them closer, but these numbers will likely never
perfectly line up, and it is probably worth tracking both, as they will
provide different insights. Frankly we've really been doing single platform
tracking so far (Facebook Ads is still really web, so not really a
different platform) - when we're looking to integrate app data into the
tracking, we will likely have a lot more instances like these where we're
comparing data that is supposedly of the same data point tracked by two
different platforms, and we'll have to validate which one makes the most
sense to use (or if we should track both ;) ).

Also, I actually don't have access to your Facebook ads account - I don't
need it, but what would be really helpful is if you could list out the
attribution models that are available to use.

Hope this helps! I'll try and loop back to a few more of these questions
before the next time we meet (I'll be back in town the week of January 9).

Hope you have a wonderful New Years!

Best,

Matthew

Hey man,

Sorry for the delay on this - been very heads down running the end-of-year
Startupbootcamp data analysis.

In terms of job remit, I could see it covering the following (very
rough/off the top of my head):

   1. Building analytics systems and processes
      - Develop quality KPI reporting on core business driving metrics
      - Creating data collection to optimize marketing/internal process
      - Aggregate data from across business units and from external sources
      to aid in strategic decision making
      - Implement mechanisms for hypothesis testing& A/B testing in
      marketing (and growth and product if necessary)
      - Create mechanisms to conduct market (internal user and external
      geographic) research to aid in decision making
   2. Digital Marketing Strategy/Optimization
      - Evaluate existing SEO execution, implement SEO best practices for
      large scale sites (loop in former head of SEO from Zoopla if necessary),
      implement or tweak procedural SEO
      - Update digital channel and platform strategy to prepare for growth
      (particularly in new markets, but also sheer content volume and team size)
      - Introduce data driven approach to digital channels
      - Create marketing infrastructure for shared templates and resources
      to allow for iterative and increasingly scalable executions
   3. Process Automation
      - Implement basic marketing automations (Zapier,
      - Spec and manage development of deeper analysis, distribution, and
      production automations (procedurally generated assets and web pages, data
      engineering projects, peripheral product strategy)
      - Look for scalable, semi or fully automatable growth engines we can
      build (likely based around SEO, partner/client engagement, or end-user
      engagement/content generation)
   4. Ecosystem/Partner/User/Business Development (AKA Other)
      - Develop relationships and processes for sourcing collaborative
      content with, locking in distribution from, and delivering reports on
      Jobbio's efficacy for them and as a whole for
clients/partners/stakeholders/management/internal
      use cases
      - Create mechanisms measure/analyze/improve templates for customer,
      client, user drip/transaction touchpoints
      - Look for opportunities to use analytics capacity to position
      ourselves as thoughtleaders in career services/recruitment industry
      - Leverage ecosystem contacts in related fields (honorCode, Emerge
      Education, Tech City UK/DBA, HiredGrad, Hired, WeWork, various events,
      various universities) for partnerships/client relationships


Times to meet (I'm out of town week of the 2nd):

   - Thursday the 12th is very flexible for me apart from 1:30-3:30pm
   - Any time the week of the 16th apart from Monday works
   - Evenings are also generally quite flexible for me


Let me know what would work! Also, I'll be in Madrid Saturday to Tuesday if
you want to grab dinner or drinks.

Hope you had a lovely christmas,

Matthew

Hey Pawel,

Was actually planning to ping you today to give you a bit of an update :)

   - Filttr
      - Piotr: Call went very well - seems like he's doing a solid job but
      that there's some underlying issues with SEO/other
infrastructure and some
      major hurdles they'll face localizing to UK, which means good opportunity
      for us. He also followed up and asked if I had suggestions for tracking
      individual campaign efficacy - I showed him a few of the simpler
templates,
      and teased him in terms of deeper analytics/execution capabilities on
      platforms like Segment, Exponea, etc. They've only just started
      client-focused marketing as well, and I don't know if they've
really looked
      at how to do cross-promotion partner based marketing (what Jobbio does
      quite well and we did a lot of at Touch Surgery). Generally, it
seems like
      there's probably a lot we could do with turning their more
flash-in-the-pan
      marketing efforts into sustainible, data driven inbound
      - Lukasz: followed up on my initial job spec that he felt like we
      could streamline it, was going to loop in someone on his team that could
      help. I'm trying to get buy in on a few projects at SBC, so
might actually
      have a project to run with
      - Proposal: was all good with this? I think we might want to sit down
      the 3 of us and hash through a template for proposals, but
seemed like this
      was okay as a first iteration?


   - Exponea
      - Michal introduced me to Peter, a biz dev consultant, who basically
      wanted me to talk to him about nailing down the messaging for how to
      communicate the benefits of Exponea over Mixpanel
      - Having lunch with one of their London biz dev managers Thursday


   - IRC: I got a proposal back yesterday, need to look through it.
   Potentially useful for our recruitment reports at Startupbootcamp, as I
   don't have time to do very much external facing research. Will be
   interesting to see what they've come up with, although I'm not sure if it
   will be comprehensive enough to justify it's price tag


   - Richard/Doctify: had an interesting call with him today. Basically
   going to send a list of names and linkedin URLs of people ranging from a
   friend who helps recruit in-house data science/ML/AI team building, the
   founder of PlusGuidance, Andy Shannon, a few other people, and see who he
   wants to meet

Let me know if you have any thoughts!

so honestly, i only really know about medtech here. likely it will lead to
better adherence to prescription regiments, easier customer management,
better diagnostics. also, research is getting easier to conduct, so you
will likely see breakthroughs coming out of smaller and smaller research
outfits.

grassroots movement and post truth could lead to skepticism around pharma
companies, which are percieved as not necessarily aligned with interests of
public welfare, particularly in the US

ageing population will likely see more medication usage as the age and as
new products and treatments are developed

Only other thing is i met a woman in a very senior role at ViiV last week,
joint-venture between GSK and someone else that's an innovation lab. Those
generally don't work.

Just thoughts

Victor interviewed me to run his growth maybe 6 months ago (connected via a
FinTech headhunter I know who seems to like me)? We had a 30 minute chat
that he cut a bit short. Then he ended up asking me to do a project that
was to execture a campaign to drive users into his platform.

My response was essentially to say that I get tons of requests to put
together campaigns for people, and given I had no real context for their
past efforts, brand identity, etc, I needed more information. He responded
that we should pause but keep in touch in the future.

I have some ideas, but finance is a tough nut to crack for inbound. Off the
top of my head, likely a mix of typical digital channels + video marketing
and thought-leadership content or tools that help everyday people with
finances to attract users interest. I also think there could be a strong
affiliate blog strategy here (think the new Chase Saphire Reserve
<http://www.pointchaser.com/no-the-chase-sapphire-reserve-is-not-the-best-credit-card-ever/>
or other referral heavy products/services typical in finance, travel, etc.).

pon., 28.11.2016 o 11:52 użytkownik Matthew Eisner <matteisn@gmail.com>
napisał:

Realised i trailed off there. Also, will add my notes about Filttr/from our
meeting later today - got a bit caught up with a hackathon at LBS/Balderton
this weekend.

Breaking down my interaction with PushDoctor and their marketing:

    - They have a great video distribution strategy - hosting YouTube
    videos, pushing them as ads, driving traction on those videos which in  
turn
    drives SEO. The doctor interviews are great content to get doctors to  
help
    push the brand (although something more thought leadership-ey/medically
    explanatory would likely do much better).


    - BIG ISSUE: they do a terrible job **ON THE MESSAGING/CONTENT OF THEIR
    VIDEOS - THEY DO NOT FRONTLOAD IMPORTANT INFORMATION, AND VIDEOS ARE TOO
    LONG**


    - Very responsive social media (although couldn't help me as I was
    pointing their video content didn't convey the core value prop until a
    minute and a half into it :D )
    - Landing page is way to cluttered, get people as far down the funnel as
    possible without giving them useless information. Same problem with their
    videos.





Also, some feedback from the surgeons at Touch Surgery:

Costas: I've heard of them and they seem to be fitting a niche... it will
become more relevant in the next 5 years or so when privatisation takes
hold and overseas people will find it difficult to access the NHS through
local GPs. Already in certain areas of the UK, overseas people are being
asked for a electric services bill (etc) for proof of residence and their
passport to access emergency health and routine surgical services. They
have a good selection of specialties and a good number within those
specialties of the specialists. UX is lovely - I don't think I could fault
it. It's comprehensive and not at all over whelming for the variety of
potential products it could have...

Ali: I tried their website, it's quite simple to use. Actually it was not
obvious how to filter and the main page was like a profile page while the
the search was more like a side thing

   drives SEO. The doctor interviews are great content to get doctors to help
   push the brand (although something more thought leadership-ey/medically
   explanatory would likely do much better).
   - BIG ISSUE: they do a terrible job
   - Very responsive social media (although couldn't help me as I was
   pointing their video content didn't convey the core value prop until a
   minute and a half into it :D )
   - Landing page is way to cluttered, get people as far down the funnel as
   possible without giving them useless information. Same problem with their
   videos.


Breaking down PlusGuidance's ideal strategy

   - They wanted to build heavily doctor profiles and do local SEO indexing
   and targeting. At a site thats more than 10,000 pages, I would recommend
   this guy (his agency <https://www.bluearray.co.uk/> - former head of SEO
   for Zoopla, which 50% of their growth could be attributed to organic
   growth). But anyways, they never really were able to get the therapists to
   start using the pages or centralizing any of their business processes onto
   the platform, largely because they did have significant demand to be able
   to incentivize it
   - Were starting to push towards developing some appointment management
   tools once they get a bit more solid footing re: revenue, as many
   therapists ended up using the platform to augment touchpoints with their
   patients and for new patient inbound, as opposed for regular appointments
   with patients (where they would make solid recurring rev)


Touch Surgery Organic Content and Partner Strategy

   - I implemented a similar content strategy at Touch Surgery to
   PlusGuidance with a few key differences - the main one being the content
   was topic focused (i.e. around surgical procedures) as opposed to person
   focused (around individuals).
      - We still prominently featured the content authors, their associated
      institutions (who were much more useful in terms of cross promotion), and
      partners, but was not indexed this way for organic search purposes.
      - This took the form of procedurally generated web pages, copy, and
      images, and well as more manually created videos, and a templated process
      for distribution. I talked to one of the Marketing Managers I hired to
      replaced me yesterday, and he informed me they will now be formally
      charging their med device clients for this service.
   - Our content eventually became extremely powerful from on organic
   traffic and banklink building standpoint, and even let to some universities
   and professors reaching out to us about publishing
   - Good god their homepage is a mess.
   - It looks like they've made some good blog content, but they're doing
   an awful job of helping it get traction (no subdirectories in blog, very
   poor interlinking of content,


Thoughts on Doctors On Demand Strategy

   - I think a little research could go a long way for messaging.
   Specifically, what are users really looking for in an on-demand doctor.
   Information to filter? To manage their appointment setting?



Ideas for Doctify

   - They do a pretty solid job in terms of front end UX and interlinking,
   which has significant SEO benefits and makes the more content driven SEO
   aspects of the strategies I listed above very powerful.
      - However, they don't aggregate doctor's blog articles on their
      portfolios, which would seem a very natural thing to do from a UX and
      doctor engagement standpoint.
   - They also have pretty solid informational medical content on their
   website, although they could likely drive doctor engagement and even better
   content by sourcing these pages from them, and nudge them to help share
   their work that's hosted on doctify, create better external backlinks
   (beneficial from SEO rank and traffic flow standpoints, poor content
   organization on blog)
   - However, they have done a poor job implementing some basic SEO best
   practices (really bad URL naming, at risk for keyword stuffing - I could
   also see some major issues with how pages are being read by Google, but
   would need access to their Google Search Console to verify)
      - They do a good job implementing other, often more complex SEO
      strategies (location targeting particularly, potentially)
   - Basically, I see Doctor profiles and general site structure and naming
   to potentially be very solid scalable wins for them (the former a bit more
   process driven, the later more of a one-off quick win).
   - Some of the worst PageSpeed site scores I have ever seen:
   https://developers.google.com/speed/pagespeed/insights/?url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.doctify.co.uk%2F&tab=mobile
   - Social executions are too complex - these are patient oriented, they
   should be simple, but medically valid
   - Really poor video strategy and mediocre execution, which is probably
   best form of content. Process to engage doctors around this to create
   content could be really beneficial.
   - In general, marketing should be more about deliver of patient value,
   although would be good to know how they target doctors and if they have
   problems there.
   - Plenty of opportunity to scrape


Questions for Doctify

   - How are they currently sourcing their blog content? Looks like largely
   from doctors, but how streamlined is this process? Do the doctors pay for
   this?
   - What do their engagements with doctors typically look like?
   Onboarding? Customer success? Cross-promotion and enabling doctors to
   evangelise platform (or are they receptive to this)?
   - Are they having more trouble driving supply or demand side, and
   acquisition or retention/engagement?
   - What are your end user touchpoints? Email automations, push
   notifications, etc?
   - Are they doing anything in the realm of academic research? Maybe
   around treatment efficacy with digital engagement, telemedicine, etc?
   - Do they have know CAC/CTL/best channels/general metrics about their
   platform, how they're acquiring and retaining their best users, etc?

date: 2016-11-16
to: "Paweł Tomczuk" <pawel.m.tomczuk@gmail.com>
subject: Bio and Sports Ecomm idea
msg_id: 1586f3634b405773
---

This is going to be a bit long:

*So I've been thinking about the ecommerce platform* - I see 3 potential
routes in terms of analysis/automation in the vein of Exponea. There are
likely some other backend components to these systems, but in terms of core
analysis and automation:

   1. Exponea
      1. Pros: could be an excellent solution, pretty low cost
      comparatively, they will likely spend a fair amount of time attempting to
      ensure customer success
      2. Cons: risky in terms of potential for platform failure
   2. CRM/Automation Solution (Marketo, Hubspot, Active Campaign)
      1. Pros: similar to exponea, maybe a bit more expensive and a more
      feature rich
      2. Cons: potentially less room to grow with a company like this that
      is already industry standard
   3. BI platform (Looker?) + automation platform (Silverpop, Pardot,
   Dotmailer, SendGrid, etc)
      1. Pros: very powerful solution, widely validated approach in terms
      of other companies using it
      2. Cons: creates significant switching costs, likely very expensive
      (although using something like Segment or Metabase instead of
Looker could
      decrease this)
   4. In house data scientist + full stack developer as data/automation team
      1. Pros: likely the most accurate solution in terms of data quality,
      facilitates quickly developing new analysis/automation, allows for
      incremental build
      2. Cons: potentially the most expensive solution, requires sourcing
      and management of team


*A few other ideas:*

   - Wiser <https://www.wiser.com/>: automated pricing and inventory
   personalization for ecommerce shops
   - Jobbio Marketing
      - Great at:
         - Eating their own dog food (using their platform to source talent)
         - Lots of industry thought leadership (content marketing, events
         production - they put on a pretty sizeable event called EXPAND every 6
         months or so)
         - Very driven around client success, lots of follow up and manual
         effort to ensure client is happy, understands product offering
         - Hijacking SEO: highly streamlined process for collecting user
         generated content from their clients and iterating web pages
from it. they
         also try and push their clients to embed iframes in their site, which
         (debatably) provides search rank improvement, but at least
creates a user
         hook.
      - Could improve on:
         - Being more targeted - they try EVERYTHING - I imagine it would
         be more cost effective to try everything, but then scale back on what
         doesn't work, which I'm not sure they do (or maybe its the
onmi-channel
         aspect that makes it work for them)
         - Overly manual - all of their content processes are completely
         manual, despite having structured data around the content they are
         producing and their clients are producing for them their
disposal at a huge
         scale
         - Understanding their customers more, making it easier to action
         items for them. They constantly ask me to integrate something on our
         website, which I constantly tell them we won't be able to do.
They should
         remember this interaction. They also are often guilty of
flooding my inbox,
         which drowns out the most important action i should follow up
with them on



*You had asked about my research experience:*

   - Ann Arbor T-Shirt Company - basic internal financial research and
   digital advertising analytics for a small t-shirt printing company
   - PRIME Research Group - conducted media research, coding, and report
   creation for banking and aviation clients (Boeing, Delta, HSBC, JP Morgan,
   etc)
   - UofM Social Psychology Department (Heath, Attitudes, and Influences
   Lab) - supported Dr. Allison Early conduct research on political viewpoint
   change (particularly around gun control) and testing-and-treatment
   behaviour of high risk demographic groups for HIV/AIDS. Developed outline
   for state of Michigan public awareness campaign by applying marketing
   principles to community health engagement
   - UofM Ross Marketing Department (Behavioral Lab) - supported Katharine
   Burson, Robert Smith, and Megan Whitmer conduct consumer
   behaviour/judgement and decision making research (particularly around
   charitable giving, perception of value based on entiativity, physiological
   factors on decision making and inhibition, etc. Often led technical
   projects, ran participants through lab experiments, processed and analyzed
   experiment data.
   - UC Berkeley Haas Marketing Department (Behavioral Lab) - supported
   Minah Jung conducting research on Pay What You Wish and other alternative,
   especially pro-social, revenue models
   - Incident Technologies - ran survey-based study with large sample on
   music learning habits to uncover trends in effective learning
   - Touch Surgery - collaborated with Medical Team lead to provide support
   applying principles from behavioural/psychology/tech research in order to
   run a meta-analysis on medical simulation and propose a foundation for the
   conducting of future research with improved validity and consistency. Then
   helped develop a process through which we supported researchers at
   Imperial, Stanford, etc to use the Touch Surgery platform to conduct
   medical simulation research on


*And my bio: *
Matthew Eisner is a growth and analytics consultant with over 7 years of
experience managing omni-channel digital campaigns, creating scalable
marketing processes, and developing data analytics capacity for companies
around the world. His approach to consulting minimizes burn rate, optimizes
for ROI, and delivers scalable solutions that allow innovative companies to
flourish. Based in London with USA/UK/EU work authorizations, Matthew works
with clients full- time, part-time, and on per contract basis around the
world to grow their exposure and impact.
I could certainly get together a longer one - I imagine I should anyways :)

date: 2016-11-14
to: Clem Hobson <clem@beeline.co>
subject: Re: WP Plugin and meeting next week
msg_id: 1586358994219342
---

Hey Clem,

Awesome! I've kicked it over to the developer, and we should have all our
goals set up by the end of this week :)

I'll build some preliminary filtering around the sheet you sent me, but
let's definitely hash through it and make sure we're on the same page and
discuss any potential hiccups that could emerge.

Re: campaign level analytics, this is a pretty simple setup - we'd
basically just take on of the tabs we're using for referrals currently, and
make the rows campaign instead of source (as it currently is). Actually,
this will likely be a better solutions once we've implemented clean
tracking URLs.

Re: Tom's influencer marketing thoughts - very astute :) This is a recent
thing, and people are really unsure about the degree or effect it will
take. Google has always had a "penalize-paidfor-backlinks" policy, but it
clearly did not work in the past, as it was widespread "grey-hat" practice.
Recently, they have gone as far to say incentivizing backlinks to your site
via free product demos or trials (a common practice in influencer blogging,
especially for new product companies) will no longer boost your SEO.
Whether they actually act upon this this activity or not is open for debate
(from the tests I've run recently, I think these links still help and I
certainly don't think they penalized yet), although they likely will
gradually move in that direction over the next 2 or 3 years. However, this
is purely about Search Rank - in terms of natural UX, you should absolutely
be trying to drive good backlinks that will drive evergreen inbound. High
level, my advice is say try and create a good process for getting bloggers
to backlink and smooth any friction points without paying before engaging
in paid backlink placements - or focus on building a true affiliate sales
model :)

Sorry for the little essay there - I love good questions like that though :)

Best,

Matthew

date: 2016-11-11
to: "Paweł Tomczuk" <pawel.m.tomczuk@gmail.com>
subject: Re: simple request for my own needs
msg_id: 15850b2808795d74
---

So I've dug into a few APIs (and lack of APIs) of some rental booking
platforms - AirBnB's is quite restrictive - no email address. Also, AirBnB,
Holidu, and most other platforms obfuscate email addresses on the front
end, and have very difficult UI's to scrape via html crawlers. They're
messaging interfaces don't present email addresses (although could
potentially be accessed at scale via API to send messages, although would
likely be red-flagged as spam very quickly). Booking.com does have emails
sometime, although they are mainly generic business inquiry email lines.

Booking.com is mainly hotels - do you want more hospitality/property
management contacts or independent/part-time renters with single or a
second vacation property?

It seems like at the most basic level, you're looking to have a touch point
with rental suppliers. I think there might be some AIrBnB renter
forum/communities, social news (Quora, Reddit, etc.) that could at least
garner solid inbound early on.

I'd have to hear a bit more, but my initial thought is that emails from a
2-sided marketplace platform would be very difficult in any way that
wouldn't be totally black hat (i.e. IP phishing, etc). You might have more
luck with trying to scrape phone numbers for an SMS/call campaign? Or I
might have some other ideas depending on the target demographic - I could
see you being able to scrape some traditional bed and breakfast owner's
emails via traditional web directories, full time independent rental
property managers via forums, etc.

subject: Tracking Solution for GA
msg_id: 1582762ddc7533f0
---

Good news!

There's a better solution for this than URL tracking. Could you please have
the developers install this plugin:
https://en-gb.wordpress.org/plugins/duracelltomi-google-tag-manager/

Then if you could perform these steps:


   1. Upload duracelltomi-google-tag-manager-for-wordpress to the
   /wp-content/plugins/ directory
   2. Activate the plugin through the 'Plugins' menu in WordPress
   3. Go to Settings / Google Tag Manager and enter your Google Tag Manager
   container ID and setup additional options

This will allow us to directly connect WooCommerce to Google Tag Manager :)

Best,

Matthew

date: 2016-10-31
to: Tom Putnam <tom@beeline.co>, Clem Hobson <clem@beeline.co>
subject: Follow up from meeting 31/10/2016
msg_id: 1581d04244893f3a
---

Hey Tom and Clem,

Just wanted to follow up with some additional info and actions from our
call today.


First, please find below a proposed URL structure for the checkout process:

   - Shop Home Page - beeline.co/shop
   - Product Info Page - beeline.co/shop/*[PRODUCT NAME]*
   - Customer Info Page - beeline.co/shop/*[PRODUCT NAME]/*Info-*[UNIQUE
   ID]*
   - Confirmation Page - beeline.co/shop/*[PRODUCT NAME]/*conf-*[UNIQUE ID]*

Where:

   - *[PRODUCT NAME] *= a code for the name of the product being viewed/in
   cart
   - *[UNIQUE ID]* = a randomly unique ID for visitors that will be paired
   to BeeLine product data

If you could please confirm with the web developers if they can do this,
that would be very appreciated. If not, the person who I'm working with to
set up the GA goals has said that he could implement this as well, and has
very reasonable rates.


Please find linked the Mobile-First Landing Page best practices deck
<https://docs.google.com/presentation/d/1PH_eerAM07AdyQdnGgyHTIYY3fx4BqxJYxmJulLrC6I/edit>.
You can see some screenshots and basic analysis of mobile landing pages,
although the focus is more desktop.


Leading up to our meeting next week on Tuesday, I will be:

   - Getting GA Goal tracking all set up and tested
   - Mapping Google Search Console data into the analytics tracking sheet
   - Adding conversion rate to source detail tab
   - Setting up basic goal conversion GA dashboard


Let me know if there's anything I'm missing or you have any questions!

Best,

Matthew

to: Tom Putnam <tom@beeline.co>
subject: Re: Tag manager code for BeeLine
msg_id: 158030f63df8da47
---

Hi Tom,

I've read through documentation, which I've linked for reference
<https://support.google.com/tagmanager/answer/6102821?hl=en#setupForWeb>,
and this looks to be quite a simple setup on your end.


Could you please have someone do the following:

   - Insert the following snippet as high up in the <head> block of your
   website theme template as possible:
   - <!-- Google Tag Manager -->
      <script>(function(w,d,s,l,i){w[l]=w[l]||[];w[l].push({'gtm.start':
      new Date().getTime(),event:'gtm.js'});var
      f=d.getElementsByTagName(s)[0],
      j=d.createElement(s),dl=l!='dataLayer'?'&l='+l:'';j.async=true;j.src=
      'https://www.googletagmanager.com/gtm.js?id='+i+dl;f.
      parentNode.insertBefore(j,f)
      <https://www.googletagmanager.com/gtm.js?id=%27+i+dl;f.parentNode.insertBefore(j,f)>
      ;
      })(window,document,'script','dataLayer','GTM-57643L');</script>
      <!-- End Google Tag Manager -->


   - Insert the following snippet as high up in the <body> block of your
   website theme template as possible:
   - <!-- Google Tag Manager (noscript) -->
      <noscript><iframe src="https://www.googletagmanager.com/ns.html?
      id=GTM-57643L"
      height="0" width="0" style="display:none;
      visibility:hidden"></iframe></noscript>
      <!-- End Google Tag Manager (noscript) -->


Once this is in place, it should take about 3 or 4 days to set up the goal
tracking, so sooner the better.

Great catching up today, and see you on Monday!

Best,

Matthew

Hi Peter,

Basically i'm looking to create a view that has 3 goal sets. Site is built
on Wordpress, Ecommerce on WooCommerce (beeline.co)

1 goal set is ecommerce - basically a goal for each type of product
purchase from the woo commerce shop, which would likely require Tag Manager
and custom tags (or I could see doing a GA Ecommerce setup instead - open
to recommendations).

set 2 would be general web conversions - goals for newsletter signups,
contact form submissions, bounces to company social media sites, etc

set 3 would be a conversion funnel for the purchase process. if you know of
a better way to do this, would love to hear, but all i've been able to do
in the past is just have an additional goal set to map the funnel.

it's very important that the system be pretty clean so we can build on top
of it in the future. I actually know how to do all of this, but have about
2 or 3 more of these projects i'm working on and a bunch more in the
pipeline, so looking to find someone who i can outsource some of the more
technical work to so i can focus on scaling clients

i'll get a spec together over the weekend and send it along and then we can
hop on a call sunday or early next week to see what you think?

Matthew

Hey man,

Can you create a consistently structured query that will pull data on a
monthly basis (i.e. each row is a date range spanning one month, 1st to
last day) with columns for the following statistics:

   1. # of Documents created
   2. # of Documents published
   3. # of documents read
   4. # of pages created
   5. # of pages published
   6. # of pages read
   7. # of total users with accounts on Relayto
   8. # of total company pages on Relayto
   9. # of seconds spend on Relayto by all users
   10. # of document shares
   11. # of total active users logged in in date range

I can then map it to the metric tracking sheet I use, we can run the query
monthly, I can simply replace the csv, and it will populate the other
sheets in the spreadsheet and equations, stats, and graphs will
automatically update.

Hey all,

Great to meet in person today! Just wanted to follow up on a few points:

A few follow actions:

   - Implement Google Search Console/Webmaster Tools and share access with
   Matthew
      - http://www.bruceclay.com/blog/set-up-google-search-console/
      - https://support.google.com/webmasters/answer/6001104?hl=en
      - https://support.google.com/analytics/answer/1308621?hl=en
   - Create fake discount code so Matthew can run through checkout process
   - Matthew to look into Woocommerce transactional email analytics
   - Matthew discuss any complications of app relation to inbound channels
   - Matthew to send along deck of evaluations of best practices for
   Mobile-First website (dated about a year or two though)
   - Matthew to update proposals/contract/timelines and send to Tom


Roadmap:

   1. Wrapup of kickoff, access permissions, proposal update contract
   signatures
   2. Begin creating benchmarking spreadsheet to map various data, begin
   funnel construction, begin Google Analytics dashboard implementation, UTM
   tracking code constructor/system
   3. Walk through systems with Clem, build out second GA dashboard,
   populate data into becnhmarking spreadsheet, ensure GA goal tracking
   working properly
   4. Tie in more complicated/less accessible data hubs and create
   additional funnels (Branch, App data, etc), sanity-check incoming data for
   validity/accuracy
   5. Evaluate extended solutions for deeper analysis (and potentially
   automation), look to tie marketing data together with in-product data for
   deeper analysis and optimization

I also assume that there might be some random stuff that comes up that I
can drop in and help on - App store listing optimization, SEO health
checks/overhauls, etc, that I'm happy to provide quick feedback on. If it
seems like a lot of work might be prudent in one of those areas, we can
expand the proposal to include it.


Questions:

   - Is the app currently available in stores?
   - Do you have wireframes for the apps I can see?


A few of the tools I mentioned today:

   - Branch <https://branch.io/>
   - Exponea <http://exponea.com>
   - Keboola <http://www.keboola.com>
   - Geckoboard <https://www.geckoboard.com>
   - App Annie <http://appannie.com>
   - Google Developers PageSpeed Tool
   <https://developers.google.com/speed/pagespeed/>


I'll follow up with an updated proposal with timelines and contract
tomorrow, and then we can get cracking!

Best,
'
Matthew

to: Karim Kefi <karim@beeline.co>
subject: Re: BeeLine Analytics project proposal
msg_id: 1577c860492f234c
---

Hi Karim,

Well, I think that really depends on what you're after.

I could create a relatively streamlined system such as the ones I sent
along in my initial proposal. Most of this would probably be pretty easy to
port over to you new implementation, and would at least get you started
benchmarking some data and give you some more transparency on user flows.
Just prior to launch of the new website, myself or your developers can
reassign goals and tracking codes so that minimal data is lost in the
transition. Additionally, the tracking could be fleshed out to include
newly introduced features at really any pace once on the new website.

More generally, if you're looking for a long term solution with more robust
analysis potential from the get go, it might be better to get one of my
data science partners involved from the get-go and get off of Google
Analytics as your analysis hub. This is especially true if you're looking
to link user purchase data to user usage data for analysis purposes.
However, I could implement a wider solution on Google Analytics
encompassing all the pages you mentioned all at once. This would likely be
a bit more cost effective (maybe 20%) than building incrementally, but a
larger payment at once. I would need a more detailed look at what would be
on each individual page before I could be sure, in order to know what would
be worth tracking.

The other factor I see here is your speed of development. If you forsee
this being a week project, it's probably best to just wait. If you see it
being a month or two (which likely equates to 3 in developer time :) ), it
might be useful to go ahead and implement so you have something in place.

Let me know what you think - happy to hop on a call and answer any
questions you might have!

Best,

Matthew

date: 2016-09-29
to: Tariq Aris <tariq@drinki.com>
subject: Re: Analytics Update
msg_id: 157760a4525286de
---

Hi Tariq,

I just want to clarify that I am not looking to dive into your social data,
I'm hoping to deliver an MVP analytics tracking solution that provides
foundations to build more robust, automated system from, and allow for
basic correlation of usage metrics and marketing activities in order to
optimize your efforts in marketing and UX.

The spreadsheet I sent you was the beginnings of essentially mapping all
your important data across disparate platforms into a single consolidated
hub. This will allow us to lay the framework for our system, run some basic
analysis to see where we should dive deeper, and ensure we prototype our
data reporting so we don't spend large amounts of time creating a
tech-heavy solution that won't meet your needs (or is missing important
data). It will include data from social platforms, web traffic, SEO
performance, developer console stats, app annie, and mixpanel, and begin to
map these into a consolidated user flow report. I started with the social
and web because it's the most standardised and lets me get a feel for some
of the messages and actions you're trying to drive hardest in your outbound
marketing efforts.

Regarding Mixpanel, I expect there to be an entire sheet of the spreadsheet
I sent you tabulating statistics from Mixpanel (which will require some
surface development of reports, segments, and formulas on Mixpanel). I can
then quickly run through these datapoints with your developer in order to
assure we're capturing the Mixpanel data we need (and tweak for more
relevant data) and strip out some of the redundant tracking
functionalities. By tracking all Mixpanel data, app store data, social
data, and web data on a single platform, we can attempt to correlate
marketing activities to growth or other KPIs.

After that, we could build out more robust analytics solution on a data
warehousing/processing/analysis stack (even just Mixpanel) to automate the
updating of data, capture data on a more granular level, and draw
conclusions from said data more easily. However, I would not recommend
Mixpanel for that. At the point when you're looking to process and relate
data from multiple platforms, Mixpanel usually becomes very difficult. I'm
getting a bit granular, but that's a more thorough summary of my vision for
the project developing.

I hope this gives a clearer idea of my thinking - would be great to hear
your thoughts and any way I can reprioritize to meet your needs more
effectively!

Let's just plan for tomorrow at 2:30.

Best,

Matthew

subject: Re: Catching up
msg_id: 1574ceb881869a40
---

Cool - well the biggest hole I see is that you simply aren't tracking high
level data in any sort of consistent way. This is a super easy fix that
I've done for countless companies.

Some of the chains you're mentioning should be simple to create and can go
into that initial tracking hub. However, there are a lot of redundant
variables and oddly grouped events that could make some of these chains
very ugly (i.e. there are over 100 different login events, about 5
different CTA events, about 6 redemption events, etcetc). These should
definitely be consolidated in logical ways before investing too much time
into building a deep analytics implementation, both for the sake of
accuracy and ease of implementation. But I think this is fine, as we can
approach it incrementally.

This is the main reason I want to make sure someone from your tech team is
in on this meeting, so someone can speak to how events are managed in that
app and passed to Mixpanel.

Thursday at 3:30 sounds great - see you in RWE then!

Best,

Matthew

to: Alex Shevelenko <alex@glocalpartners.com>
subject: Re: Thoughts on their CTA ?
msg_id: 156fa7872693705b
---

i didn't even register that it was a sample email - i like the "send me an
example" - i think we could do one better by saying "upload a pdf" and
we'll send you a sample of a similar one - then we could go above and
beyond if it's someone we actually want to work with or a quick production
win and actually make the sample THEIR pdf. or just deliver a similar one.

i think specifically on zembula's page, this CTA is lost to me by them
having a Request a Demo CTA at the top and bottom (first and last are
usually the most mentally salient information positions). I like the send
me an example CTA much more than the request a demo, even if they're the
same thing. Request a demo makes me think I have to jump on a call, and I
get at least 20 requests for these sort of calls from martech/adtech/etc
companies per month.

subject: Re: Thoughts on their CTA ?

---

i like how they have a CTA on almost every "fold", and how they vary a bit
(although request a demo is the most frequent).

i think overall it's a pretty clean and typical landing page, nothing wild,
but pretty simple, easy to understand. i think that the hero image (header
image/gif) doesn't provide enough context on what the product acutally is
that i'm looking to get a demo on, which i see as a potential major
improvement on a page like this.

i do like that its a relatively typical in page layout - makes finding the
info you're looking for very quick.

i also think that for certain clients, a demo could be a major way to sell
them, and can generate more hot leads who will expect a touch point.
however, i think that me personally, I hate when people try to sell to me
via phone (i would MUCH prefer email), and the idea of doing a product demo
is a huge turnoff for me - I have a feeling that's not true for older
generations (and likely the opposite).

date: 2016-08-29
to: Cleopatra Lawrence <lawrencecleopatra@gmail.com>
subject: Career/Job Hunting Resources
msg_id: 156d755cc97afcda
---

*Start:*

   - CV - top 10% of rising grad CVs I see (apart from not so much work
   experience). Little nitpicky stuff like removing numerical dates from
   wimbledon. How can you pull these different roles/experiences together to
   make it sound like you've always been on the path to do a job like X?
   - What do you want to do? Now? Long-term? What are your personal goals?
   - Startup, corporate, SME, NGO, Government, Policy, Academia?
   - Location? Particularly important right now. Lots of factors at play
   here personally, professionally, and long-term vs short-term
   - Job type?
   - Future goals?
   - Spreadsheets to track!


*Where to Look:*

   - Angellist
   - School career counselling
   - LinkedIn - industry standard. mass invite is a good idea. great way to
   research, reach out to people, lay groundwork.
   - Tech City Jobs Board
   - Jobbio (I have friends here who can likely help you)
   - HiredGrad (I have friends here who can likely help you)
   - Guardian Jobs
   - Indeed


*Tactics:*

   - My deck: https://docs.google.com/presentation/d/
   1BNpVpTQc9YwThmo6tznKnEm1g5lkFDguHZ89CMJdEYw/edit?usp=sharing
   <https://docs.google.com/presentation/d/1BNpVpTQc9YwThmo6tznKnEm1g5lkFDguHZ89CMJdEYw/edit?usp=sharing>
   - Reach out to people on LinkedIn at companies that interest you and
   just say you're interested in what they do and want to hear more to know if
   it's something you'd like to pursue as a career path
   - Ask people for advice
   - Send a quarterly or biannual newsletter to you personal network
   letting them know what you've been up to (I can't tell you how huge this
   can be in 3 to 4 years time if you keep up on it)


*Overarching notes:*

   - Hunting for a job is marketing yourself and the value you can add to a
   business
   - Norms of recipricority
   - Narrative and storytelling is huge. Getting the other person to like
   you is often even more so
   - Play off people's egos
   - Risk aversion in hiring
   - Figure out what they want and change your message
   - If you really want it, deliver value before you join, force them to
   hire you
   - Good jobs have an element of personal network to them - the best jobs
   I've gotten have been through a referral
   - The British Paradox

---

Hi Edward (or do you prefer Ed?),

Sorry for the delay - it's been a crazy week kicking off a data pipeline
automation project with a part-time hire I brought on.

So this mostly looks really interesting and up my alley - a lot of the
points are core specialties of mine. I think I'm lacking a bit in some of
the more technical areas, particularly when it comes to setting up new
development environments (it's much easier for me to augment a system
that's already been implemented, especially if it's been done cleanly). I
usually rely on collaborating with internal development teams or speccing
and managing projects with outsourced development to make up for that. I
see a lot of potential to come in and immediately make impact, as well as
embed marketing into the platform itself over time, which is always a lot
of fun.

I'm also quite eager to improve my technical skills - necessity is a
catalyst for knowledge for me, and the limited working proficiency I have
in HTML/CSS (well, I'm actually pretty well versed there), JS/JQuery, PHP,
and Python has all stemmed from the immediate need to learn it to complete
a project. I'm actually in a bit of a phase of trying to ramp up my Python
data analysis skills for the data pipeline project I mentioned above, as
well as to automate some marketing metric reporting systems I've created in
the past. Frankly I think that I would probably have more need to continue
learning in more technical topics at a startup than at Startupbootcamp,
which is a big reason I've been starting to look around.

I do think you'd have a lot of trouble finding someone truly an expert in
all the areas you're looking for. If you want someone who's more primarily
a developer, and marketing-second, my flatmate actual fits that bill and is
in the job market. However, he'd be lacking a bit in some of the analytics,
production, and digital strategy areas. Or I certainly have a few other
marketing-first growth hackers I could also intro you to, although they
will almost assuredly be less technical than I am.

Re: Wednesday: I'm free pretty much all day - I could drop by your office
around lunchtime or towards the end of the day if that might work? Let me
know what's ideal on your end.

   <http://www.surveygizmo.com/s3/2633402/521e8800f82f> (housed on Survey

Hi Victor,

Sorry for the delay - as I might have mentioned, I was in the USA for the

etc.

If you'd like me to do the exercise, I'd like to first speak to your other
founder(s?). It's the harsh reality that I've spoken to well over 50
startups in seeking my next role, in hopes that it will be my last startup
role. If I signed up for all of them, let alone did projects for them, I
wouldn't be able to keep up with my role managing our startup recruitment
at Startupbootcamp. I consider the problem being addressed, the team
working on it, and usage metrics to be much better indicators of startup
potential than a product itself, particularly at early stage.

I have essentially rejected every startup I've looked at thus far as being
too late stage or having too little potential. That's is part of why more
recently, I've started looking towards VC and corporate innovation
consulting jobs. However, I'm way too much of a workaholic to enjoy that
more than a job at a startup I truly love working for and believe I can
help achieve success. So when Pablo said he had an interesting company to
talk to, I figured I'd see what you were up to - and it does seem
interesting.

All to say, in order for me to justify the kind of investment I would need
to make in terms of my time and the immediate value I would deliver to you,
I need a better idea of your traction, terms of the position, tools that
are in place (email, web systems, platform engagement mechanisms, tracking
points, past data, etc), hear a bit more about your longer term vision, and
to meet your other cofounder.

Happy to come in and chat again sometime!

Best,

Matthew

date: 2016-07-22
to: Idan Beck <idanbeck@gmail.com>
subject: Re: Opinion on a startup
msg_id: 15612e9b6c5a99f9
---

Well so I'm actually doing very applied project - basically working on a
solution to automate interaction between a network of twitter accounts (and
other little twitter odds and ends). I've actually got a bit of it up and
running, but it's super buggy so just working on cleaning it up a bit for
now. Would be good to apply ML to it though.

Before that I was building some super low production value websites and
then knocking around a bit with my own. And have been through about 25% of
codecademy, although that's only been marginally helpful - too sandboxed.
But I've been doing quite a lot with web tracking, analytics, and technical
marketing over the past 2 years, and was getting really limited by my lack
of more hands on skills. Plus I had dabbled when I was younger, so was just
a matter of getting started again.

So what I know about Mimi:
-About 300k tests performed
-60% second week retention rate
-LTV and CAC are still largely undefined - and anecdotally, it seems
European companies are really bad at tracking this (I set calculations up
for Touch Surgery for this, and generally it seems like their investors
were apparently okay with having them poor data here - although maybe
explains the troubles in raising their B round)
-Their initial strategy is build out partnership integrations with
Soundcloud, Apple Music, Spotify
-Have raised €4mil in funding so far
-Are supposedly in contact with Kleiner Perkins, Atomica, Google Ventures,
looking to close another round in fall
-Current revenues are minimal, and supposedly their existing investor
-Equity structure has >50% held for mgmt/staff
-Have a stong medical/academic advisory, and a few PhD in auditory related
fields on the team
-Seem more technically competent than most
-I've had success growing userbase for medical apps in scalable and
sustainable ways. They seem very aligned from a marketing strategy
standpoint, which is good. However, I also see this move as potentially
pigeon holing myself.
-Monetization will likely be through providing information to healthcare
providers, working with venues and events, third-party integrations, etc.
They have the flexibility from their investors to hold off on trying to
generate revenue in favour of building userbase, and they seem to have a
good segment-and-test approach mentality towards implementation

I should mention, I took a very positive outlook in those points above. I'm
certainly looking to have them torn down if you don't see a good picture
there. They're certainly not the only company I'm looking at, but figure
you'd have valuable insight in this and might think of it in ways I might
not see.


In terms of DreamOS - certainly sounds interesting to me. I personally see
more long-term value in AR, but VR is obviously incredibly interesting and
a more immediately accessible opportunity. I also see a pretty linear AR
application of what you're building potentially, particularly the
development component, so would certainly be curious as to hear more about
what you're working on, what the immediate roadmap is, and what you're
thinking longer term.

In all honesty, I have found a bit of a "chasing the high" phenomena from
having worked at Incident on a product/platform that was just badass, as
compared to most of what I've found since which has largely been
underwhelming (maybe it's SF vs Europe, the startups I've been working
with, who knows). It's probably been beneficial for me having to market
products or services that maybe frankly aren't as technically innovative
and certainly has been to get experience in more diverse industries. In a
way I wish I knew some of the more applied and technical marketing that I
know now at Incident, but obviously Incident was a major step in my road to
that learning.

I'll be stateside from Tuesday next week for about 2 weeks - want to hop on
a call and catch up a bit while I'm in a more accessible time zone?

I was actually messaging with Nolan yesterday, he mentioned he enjoyed your
chat. He's probably top 3 or 4 EECS grads I know out of UofM 2013, and I
know quite a few. Certainly have a few others I could intro you to.

Things are pretty good with Dream so far - team is pretty solid (myself,

procedural sky/sun, dynamic lights, per pixel shading, even leap motion

date: 2016-07-11
to: Alex Shevelenko <alex@glocalpartners.com>
subject: Re: UNAUTHORIZED ACCOUNT
msg_id: 155dc65e94543d0c
---

So it's sort of a question of begging for forgiveness or permission. I
generally prefer forgiveness, as it can open doors. Seeing that this was
the sent by the "IT Admin", I bet he never checks this again. Not to
mention, who knows what legal footing they actually have.

I think we should allow for unlisted docs by default without payment (seems
like a good differentiator, and a lot of publishers would want to be able
to distribute internally before externally).

As per community generated content, the key is being able to incentivize
the creation of content that drives our business goals. Prepopulating the
platform can also be good to indicate a social norm, provide examples, etc.
Having some sort of structure here is pretty important. But also just
view-counts, leaderboards, and general gamification. I think theres a lot
to learn here from platforms like Wikipedia and Reddit that have
complicated creation, moderation, and ranking schemes - Wikipedia
especially given the quality of content on it. Vimeo I guess too (as this
is sort of how they try to differentiate from YouTube, as a more producer's
platform).

date: 2016-06-22
to: Michael Boyle <mike@clubhouse.cc>
subject: Potential Technology Partner Relationship
msg_id: 15578d5b0112207c
---

This might be out of your current focus, but FYI:

The College & Career Institute teacher survey results have helped me
realize that there could be an additional opportunity here.

CollegeXpress (www.collegexpress.com) is a good student resource for
students to check out post secondary institutions. I'm convinced however
that there should be an online resource that allows students to explore
different careers, receive career counseling, guide students on high school
course selections related to specific careers, link students to specialized
institutions including 2-year trade schools, etc.  In other words, I
believe students should have a better sense of their career options and
passions before choosing a post secondary institution.

The career site should be free to every middle and high school student.
(13+ yrs of age)  Revenues would be based on the following:

1.  Corporate (HR) sponsorships of online content and advertising.
Corporations are constantly trying to recruit the best talent they can
find, and the sooner they connect with teens, the better their future
recruiting chances.

2.  Even though the site would be free to every student, for a small fee
students could upgrade for added counseling., benefits, whatever.  The
annual fee could be between $4.95-$9.95, just as the Weekly
Reader publication was for years.  (The number of U.S. students alone in
grades 8-12 is approximately 24 million.)

Complementing the online career site would be our 4-day College & Career
Institutes.  As we have discussed, the 4-day Orlando model could be
replicated eventually in other parts of the country.  (71 schools have now
given me their date preference for Orlando Spring 2017!)

With our teacher database, we can continually encourage teachers to have
their students register on the site.  (5 million teacher email addresses of
which 50% are middle and high school teachers.)  Within our team we have
the talent pool of content writers, not to mention that we could outsource
so much of it.

Our biggest need is a technology partner to build and maintain the
platform.  I have talked to LinkIn, however I never could connect with the
right person....and never really wanted to tell them too much!  (Actually
our career site would be more like CollegeXpress than LinkedIn.  We don't
need students to post their profiles.)  In the meantime I have initiated
talks with 6 technology companies that could build and host the platform
based on an equity position.  (CollegeXpress being one possibility.)  The
one company that I've had a number of meetings with is called INgage
Networks.  www.ingagenetworks.com in Naples.

Would love to hear your input!

Thanks,

Lyman

I've pinged my contact at CrunchBase but haven't heard back.
So looking through the API documentation, I see a few issues -It looks like crunchbase likely only allows you API access to get peoples
social media links. Accelerators get messy but they should be under orgs - we
just need to target maybe 20 of them inititally. I'm pretty sure
people/relationships or organizations/relationships will let you retrieve data
on investors based on org/relationships and people/rel.
I'm sure there are some email plugins for name/organization, but don't know if
you use them/how cost effective they are.
For reference: -https://data.crunchbase.com/docs/organizations -https://data.crunchbase.com/docs/people -https://developer.crunchbase.com/docs
Let me know what you think! _____________________________

subject: Re: test-work
msg_id: 155094e043869782
---

Hey Marvin,
I just reread your initial email and noticed the Sunday due date - sorry for the
delay.
Please find linked my test-work . There was some vagueness in the measurement metric you provided, so I am
operating under the assumption that you're looking for me to generate 300 NEW readers WITH ACCOUNTS CREATED within one week .
I also used the assumption of a global conversion rate of 10% from reached users
to website visitors, and a 10% rate of new visitors creating an account.
Existing data you have in these areas (access to a Google Analytics dashboard,
Mixpanel dashboard, or internal stats on this) would be very helpful in
improving the model. I'd be happy to talk through what channels I intuitively I
think would be higher or lower and why as well, but wanted to keep the model
conservative for now. I could also see doing more content heavy executions
(video, interviews with the author, lists of similar books, etc) but it seems
unlikely that I would be able to do so effectively in a matter of 7 days without
preexisting infrastructure or resources.
I would also use ref tokens or UTC/UTM tracking for these campaigns so I could
readjust the channel marketing mix in subsequent campaigns.
Please let me know if you have any questions, or next steps. Also, I'm glad you
asked for this in a spreadsheet - I've always been a fan of this article , and love when a founder/startup understands how to project growth properly!
Best,
Matthew

date: 2016-05-23
to: consulting@elucidata.co.uk
subject: Startupbootcamp Data Analytics Help
msg_id: 154dd4ff12e3cb7c
---

Hi,
We're looking for some help on a really cool project - analyzing huge swatches
of data on startups around the world. We have access to some awesome data sets
(our own and third-party), but want to automate parts of our pipeline, clean up
how we store our data, and do some reporting automation.
We'd ideally like to tie our data from Google Analytics/Web, Social Media, and
Salesforce together to be able to run analysis across it. I've considered
setting up Segment.io with Periscope as a solution for this (or even something simpler like
Mixpanel). However don't have the bandwidth to set this up, or the experience to
be comfortable doing so on the scale of our business.
For context, this project is for Startupbootcamp's Global team, the oversight
and management arm of one of the 4 largest startup accelerators in the world,
with over 350 portfolio startups, 100+ corporate partners, thousands of mentors,
etc. We receive 2000+ applications to our accelerators each year, and run pretty
deep analysis on that. However, coming from a research background, I recognise
that if we were to tie this data together with the other data we collect
regarding our marketing, we could massively optimise our marketing executions
and efforts, and tying additional datasets in (we have data sharing partnerships
with Mattermark, CrunchBase, etc), we could drive some incredible analysis.
Would love to chat about how you might be able to help us!

date: 2016-05-22
to: Alex Shevelenko <alex@glocalpartners.com>, Nikita Korotaev <nikita@glocalpartners.com>
subject: GIF & Image Automation Research
msg_id: 154dacd066ff4179
---

Hey guys,

I looked in to automating GIF and image production - it looks like we could
do it via software or web-rendering. SDKs (Photoshop has one that looks
like it can handle the image production, and there are similar resources
for image-to-gif automation). There are also some python libraries and SDKs
specifically for GIF production, and I don't think rendering a browser page
as a png or jpg should be too tricky. I also found some interesting stuff
about GIF and web image optimization I included in my notes.

It would then just be a matter of figuring out what images to pull from the
doc into the template, and how to assure people upload files that will look
good - There are some cool SDKs around image recognition that could be
useful here long run that I included in my research as well below.

Find my more technical research here:
https://docs.google.com/document/d/1WRxhWcgghcfuMUa0mfZisIUAFsPcTTQoJk-1aaimGbk/edit?usp=sharing

https://docs.google.com/document/d/1rrJ2cd8RYU2s1_OnSoGqb1Z7_QNSY7dBMOD6-Za-CaU/edit?usp=sharing

Also, I had drinks with a guy who does pretty hands-on SaaS sales. Took
some notes - most might be intuitive to you but I thought some were really
interesting:
https://docs.google.com/document/d/1TuH9Ymy3XQGP3Th1DO6y-wxI7W1LfS-ZgUtxZNTfczs/edit?usp=sharing

I've also been tearing down the onboards from Canva/Hubspot (theirs is
really good) and will do a few others and really look into the onboarding
process as well again when I get some other stuff together

I've know Gregory Goltsov for about 20 months now. We first met while
working together at a company called Touch Surgery, a promising medical
tech startup in London. We have worked together on a few freelance
analytics projects for startups and medium sized businesses.

I would certainly say Greg is honest and trustworthy. In a profession often
characterized by opaque communication and misunderstanding between clients
and suppliers (early-stage software development), Greg is extremely
transparent, straightforward, and customer-oriented. In fact, I would say
Greg is my favourite software developer to work with because of this (as
well as the fact that despite his extreme intelligence, he's is wonderfully
social and engaging). I had actually offered Greg a spot in my flat, and
we're toying with starting a business together from our freelancing work.
All to say I trust Greg immensely - enough so that I would consider sharing
my home, my career, and my business with him.

I think he would make a better tenant than me in all honesty! He's more
organized and financially stable than I (and budgets his money well). He's
also generally a very open and helpful person.

I'm the Global Marketing Manager for Startupbootcamp (a network of 15
startup accelerators around the world that have invested in about 350 tech
startups). My home address is 170 Campbell Rd, E3 4ED, London.

Please let me know if there's anything else.

date: 2016-05-05
to: Gregory Goltsov <gregory@goltsov.info>, Michael Boyle <mike@clubhouse.cc>
subject: updated engagement/onboard notes for lifted/clubhouse/dataland
msg_id: 1547e3d483eb919c
---

IDEAS FOR NEXT STEPS:

-Flesh out rank infrastructure

-Reingagement campaigns/emails with auto populated content/general
reengagement hooks

-Automated social posts fro top content each day to community owners page -
what are parameters for posting, to which platforms? could even incentivise
(person who submits content gets free g each day, autopen email
notification)

-Canva onboard



*CLUBHOUSE*

1. Content Stream: Clubhouse is dominated by dada land posts - we need to
set some basic algorithm parameters for how content is populated into sub
community streams

2. Clubs page - when I go here, it's empty - there should at least be
prompts for me to add 3 or 4 top clubs. Think twitter on boarding where it
forces you to follow a few accounts. We shouldn't force people, but if
people navigate to a section of the app where their preferences will fill
in content, we need to prompt them to fill them in to start populating
content, or at least suggest a few popular options

3. I went to the Serial Club, and it seems pretty dead. I think you should
potentially start pulling in top content related to the podcast from
relevant feeds on reddit, etc, or on communities where active members
emerge, start naming moderators. also potentially asking questions after
each podcast or getting community members to rate new episodes as they're
released could help drive more significant engagement

4. App Download Icons: currently violating developer marketing guidelines,
i don't think its a big deal at the moment, but just so you're aware you
need to use the icons they give you





*DADALAND*

1. Signin/Signup button very small. process via twitter very smooth. push
people towards initial login with twitter, shorter process than Facebook (1
step vs 2 steps). Also, you should prompt people to share the community
immediately after they sign up via the platform they integrated, as well as
through additional platforms they integrate

2. Driving engagement through social norms: expose how many people have
tapped a link in the community to drive more engagement - show that
engagement is normal (normative social influence). Throw share cards into
the timeline, measure when people are most likely to engage with the card
based off of the rate at which they share and the previous actions they've
done, then serve more out after those events. show engagements across all
content (group engagement for low reactions into higher numbers to make
look bigger)

3. Ranks - Terms around Dadaland passport are super vague (at least tell a
bit of what you're looking for)- there should also be some sort of meter
that measures your progress. also, the ranks look bad without images. Would
suggest moving the leaderboard to the top and rank information to the side
maybe? I dunno, layout is weird to me. Also, I don't understand how you
accumulate points, I would lay this out clearly somewhere (also, we should
talk about what you point scales are, so as to drive people to be posting
the type of content that is most ideal to your customers/driving
engagement/the platform health). I had to post, then go back to the rank
section to figure it out - would be cool to have some sort of visible
counter next to your name as you navigate through the app, or have a
discrete little "+1 rank points" animation when you generate points by
commenting, etc.. Also, do you have popups or like a celebratory message
with a prompt to share to other social networks that they've achieved a
rank when they reach a new rank level?

4. Content stream: should be a way to filter top posts, also maybe a
dashboard of top posts of the day/month/year/all time

5. Profile completion - after onboard, have a little  notification badge a
la linkedin that tells people they're XX% through completing their onboard,
no ability to integrate a Facebook after signing up with twitter (you want
to collect as many contact points as you can). i would also eventually try
to capture an email - potentially you might want to have popups in the
newsfeed to capture deeper contact info like email, phone, that will allow
you to drive deeper engagement. we should think about what information you
really want to be collecting from people re: profile and then
optimize/gamify that. little cards in the feed that are "want to get X
points? fill this in in your profile). capture as much data as you can.

6. Notifications - there should be soft notifications as new content gets
posted to let you know when there's activity in the stream (a little number
next to activity). there should also be a personal notifications section or
tab of the platform, which notifies you as people engage with content
you've posted, or when major updates occur. these more significant
notifications should trigger emails, text messages, notification badges,
push notifications, when you reach new ranks, etc. must find way to limit
these hard notifications so as not to overwhelm people, as well as track
them to see which ones are effective for driving engagement

7. Posting: you should be able to push the post out to your linked social
networks (think instagram posting to other networks), with a link that
hooks people back in to dada land - i do like that you have a link to the
post that you can share though when you pull up the post menu after post.
camera icon is confusing - list 4 options across the bottom for content
types you want to drive that are valuable for you and platforms that a lot
of people use to pull content in from, then a button with more.

8. Events - bug when clicked on an event. is there a way for users to add
events to their calendars? set an email reminder? etc?

9. Chat - how do you find new chat threads? also, you should allow for
upvoting of messages in chat potentially

10. Sharing and referrals - you should HEAVILY incentivise on boarding new
users (and track the activity of those onboard) via referral through
points. i.e. if i bring a new user on, i get 10 points. if they post
something, i get another point. if they achieve  a rank, i receive 50
points, etc. You should have a prompt immediately after onboard to invite
friends (this message should be customisable for each company, but also
ideally tracked for eventual nlp ml processing later)



Ideas to drive deeper engagement:

-Email newsletters with top content from the past month and any promotions
they want to push. can make a contest out of being featured content for the
newsletter (i.e. top content)

-Leaderboards of top content sharers/community influencers

-Gamification (badges, etc)

---

5. Notifications - there should be soft notifications as new content gets
posted to let you know when there's activity in the stream (a little number
next to activity). there should also be a personal notifications section or
tab of the platform, which notifies you as people engage with content
you've posted, or when major updates occur. these more significant
notifications should trigger emails, text messages, notification badges,
push notifications, when you reach new ranks, etc. must find way to limit
these hard notifications so as not to overwhelm people, as well as track
them to see which ones are effective for driving engagement

6. Posting: you should be able to push the post out to your linked social
networks (think instagram posting to other networks), with a link that
hooks people back in to dada land - i do like that you have a link to the
post that you can share though when you pull up the post menu after post

7. Events - bug when clicked on an event. is there a way for users to add
events to their calendars? set an email reminder? etc?

8. Chat - how do you find new chat threads? also, you should allow for
upvoting of messages in chat potentially

9. Sharing and referrals - you should HEAVILY incentivise on boarding new
users (and track the activity of those onboard) via referral through
points. i.e. if i bring a new user on, i get 10 points. if they post
something, i get another point. if they achieve  a rank, i receive 50
points, etc. You should have a prompt immediately after onboard to invite
friends (this message should be customisable for each company, but also
ideally tracked for eventual nlp ml processing later)



Ideas to drive deeper engagement:

-Email newsletters with top content from the past month and any promotions
they want to push. can make a contest out of being featured content for the
newsletter (i.e. top content)

-Leaderboards of top content sharers/community influencers

-Gamification (badges, etc)

date: 2016-04-25
to: Pavlos Papanicolaou <pavlos@camrate.com>
subject: Re: Outline of Growth Ideas
msg_id: 1544edd3e871b396
---

Hi Pavlos,

Sorry about the delay in this message - it's been quite a crazy few weeks
for me. I think at this point, I am not the best person to guide the
execution of these growth hacks for you. Greg has also decided to go full
freelance, so I am sure he'll be interested in talking to you. I've cc'ed
him here so he see's where we're at. I can also introduce you to two other
growth hackers, one who does PPC/paid advertising, and another who does
more technical growth hacking.

I'm also happy to get involved in a more advisorial capacity for a few
hours here and there as you build out mechanisms for growth. However, I
don't have the time to currently act as a project/product/growth manager,
unfortunately, as I am taking on working with a few other clients in more
significant capacities.

I head to LA next week, and am unfortunately booked flat out til then.
Happy to hop on a Skype call next week or grab a drink or dinner after work
the following (May 9th).

Best,

Matthew

To answer your questions:

·        What we try first then next then next: Ideally, you would work on
more than one at once, so as not to put all your eggs in one basket. I
would say start with SEO/ASO, and user generated content, then move to
referral schemes/in-platform growth hacks, then more outbound type
activities like Twitter automation and PPC.

·        How long will it take to set up first then rest: That's very
difficult to say - it's more dependent on the technical development time -
in most cases it would take 5 or 10 hours to spec out the proeject.

·        How long to implement: Again, very difficult to say. Also worth
noting that tactics like SEO and ASO have a much longer lifespan (and take
a bit of time to take full effect), whereas outbound tactics like are more
of a pay-per-impression one-off execution with generally little long-term
lifespan.

·        How much time from you  and greg if any: cc'ed Greg who can tell
you more. I could put in 2 hours a week or 5 hours every two weeks on
smaller projects.

·        What you need from me re resources – this needs careful planning:
tba

·        What we gonna measure / track – what KPIS: users and time spent
per user onboarded to the platform (ideally also another metric that
includes the users THEY refer onto the platform), content creations

·        Whos gonna do what when: tba

·        What objectives / expectations to set so I can calculate expected
ROI (eg invested time o and / or cash vs. loyal users retained after 30 and
60 days) and then measure against what actually happens: I think this is a
deeper conversation. However, if I were to work on this, I would need to
insist on tying my reward/objectives in some way to users onboarded, not
loyalty/retention, as that is the focus of my efforts and thus what I
should be evaluated on.
