Hey Alex,

Just wanted to follow up on our chat today. Thanks for taking the time - I
see this as a really exciting opportunity to apply my skills in an
organisation where they would truly be valued, and something that makes a
lot of sense in terms of my interest in marketing and behaviour in digital
environments, as well as my career goals.

To follow up on a couple of points:

   - *Basic idea*: Working part time initially for equity sounds like a
   great plan until I scale in to a full time role. I would want to hear a bit
   more on what your thinking was in terms of pay, but I don't imagine this
   being an issue - wealth is not an immediately motivating factor for me
   outside of assuring my basic stability.
   - *Pioneers*: I'll find out who the judging panel is. They also might
   see the email sig placement I mention below. Tim, their MD, isn't very
   responsive, so Filip might actually be a more productive contact in terms
   of being able to get attention for long enough to pitch. Or even offering
   to build Pioneers post-event execution during your pitch could be a pretty
   unique way of reaching them/demonstrating your confidence to stand out
   during the competition. Just a thought!
   - *China Start*: I have to follow up with Bo tonight or tomorrow. I'll
   do the email sig line thing I mention below, but can also include a link
   to our demo day Relayto (assuming Aggelos has updated it a bit more). I can
   also mention it in passing next time we hop on a call (I imagine next week
   - he asked for my number in his last email - let me know if there's a way
   you'd like me to phrase what I say outside of a passing mention that we use
   Relayto and have had good results).
   - *General Alignment*: I'm planning to add the IoT doc with Intel to my
   email sig, and will be thinking of more ways to compound my executions in
   mutually beneficial ways. This should help give a subtle visibility to SBC
   staff/partners/stakeholders of how we use Relayto, as well as continue to
   drive stats on the whitepaper. And I'll think of some more ways to do this.
   I've also recently been archiving my own resources recently (personal
   contacts, various lists, document templates, valuable slide decks/articles,
   etc.), so will continue doing this for our use at Relayto.
   - *Priorities moving forward*: I want to make sure as much as possible
   my work is as valuable as possible to you/Relayto. To that end, I'll
   compiled any backlogged to-dos that have been pushed (I have them in my
   notepad) and ideas moving forward of where I think I could add significant
   value. Any suggestions, reprioritization, etc to that list (or even before)
   is greatly appreciated, or maybe it makes more sense to discuss this next
   week.

I also want to say that I really appreciate you openness over the past year
and willingness to mentor me. It makes me much more reassured in terms of
the long-term viability of what you're building, and that what you're doing
truly aligns with my interest. It also has certainly taught me a lot (and
has given me the benefit of using Relayto at TS and SBC :D ).

Hearing you say that you are building this company for your grandkids, not
a quick exit, was something that I always assumed to an extent from seeing
your approach to building the platform. Still, it was extremely comforting
to hear you conceptualize it directly today. At this point in my career in
startups, I've developed criteria for the founders I look to work with - I
think Relayto is one of only teams I've met for a long time where those
pieces are all in place (at least 2 founders, one with borderline-genius cs
skills, one with serious business acumen and past success, working on a
product with serious opportunity in a market (or looking to create a new
one ideally) with large potential-size). And most importantly to me, I see
the opportunity to build something truly groundbreaking in an area I'm
passionate about while still having opportunities to continue learning.

Anecdotally, I think the a-ha moment for me with you guys was when I told
you about the academic research . I think you're the only person outside of
academia who actually got excited about that :)

I'm showing my flat at 7:15, but happy to hop on a call later in the
evening or tomorrow to chat a bit more, or it probably makes sense for me
to drop by sometime next week.

Thanks again!

Matthew

date: 2016-04-11
to: liz@plusguidance.mail.intercom.io
subject: Re: Quick guide on finding the right therapist.
msg_id: 15405f09b36ea377
---

No problem - my main point around the length of message is the potential to
overwhelm, but your data will tell you if that's the case or not. Just off
the top of my head, it also might make sense to send a second message to
people on the chat window on the site if they don't respond to the first
one after a few minutes.

Anecdotally, we see our response rate double at Startupbootcamp when we do
a second batch outreach via LinkedIn to source our startups. Especially
with something with such high initial friction, I could see this being a
touch that changes what looks like a likely-automated message into
something that feels a bit more personal/legitimately concerned or
interested.

I only say this because I think what y'all are working on is awesome - I've
been keeping my eyes on startups in this space for a while as I am from a
psych research background once-upon-a-time, and really like the approach
you're taking. Either way if you're testing and optimizing, it sounds like
you know what you're doing :)

date: 2016-04-04
to: Pavlos Papanicoloau <pavlos@camrate.com>
subject: Outline of Growth Ideas
msg_id: 153e338020277805
---

Hi Pavlos,

Please find below an outline of various ideas and concepts I've laid out on
driving early stage growth. I'm happy to hands on execute any of these for
you with some engineering support. In terms of pricing, I could see a few
things working (ideally a mix of the following):

   - Set milestones with payout values
   - Marginal payment per acquisition (or 100)
   - Flat rate

Let me know what you think, and when might work for you to get together to
discuss. I could probably do Friday/this weekend or early next week.

Also, please find my UDID at the bottom.

Best,

Matthew


*Growth Hacks:*

*General growth hacking process:*


   - -Plan: spec out platform
   - -Execute: execute growth hack to best of intuition
   - -Measure: we'll need Google Analytics setup with solid goal tracking
   - -Optimize: apply learnings from analytics to improve next iteration
   - -Repeat: start again

*Algorithmic UGC-driven SEO flag planting*


   - -Allow for Google indexing of platform (and ideally spotlight search,
   deep public content linking (think google search results for pintrest
   posts))
   - -Using your RSS feed scrape-and-post engine, start a webpage/content
   flag planting. monitor through google webmaster tools and serve a signup pop
   - -This results in new searchable content on google and other search and
   image engines - if we can add 10 pieces of content that attract 10 new
   signups per day, this ends up being 3000 new users per month.
   - -Automation of SEO tags requires small amount of dev work, a bit of
   marketing strategy
   - -Use categories of content as subgrouping for optimization (i.e. find
   which categories are attracting the best inbound and push those hardest)

*Twitter scripted outreach*


   - -Up front costs:
   - -audience targeting - $15/month
      - -bulk tweet scheduling - 30 days free, then $99 per month
   - -Targets:
   - -users with a specific parameter or feature, create list of account
      names
      - -users who have posted a very polar post (sentiment score in
      twitter advanced search) about a brand; ask them to add their
review to the
      platform (or scrape them in)
   - -send out "beta" invites to the platform (up to 10k per day), use
   bit.ly tracking links or google analytics UTC/ref codes to measure
   efficacy
   - -Probably better for general brand awareness than acquisition

*Referral/affiliate strategy*: a good referral or affiliate scheme takes
the burden of customer acquisition off of you


   - -Allow people to use CamRate content as an embeddable poll - this
   drives votes on the content on camrate, as well as new users in to the
   platform
   - -Leverage influential brands and users on the platform to spread
   word/drive signups
   - -I could see brands loving a consumer survey application, which
   allowing for early polling and user access to data would help drive
   significantly, as well as to piggyback on third party b2c marketing
   executed by bigger brands
   - -What value can you provide to brands and users to incentivise
   referrals? at least a bade (make it clear what its for to drive people to
   unlock it)

*Platform cross population strategy*


   - -Find a platforms where you can seed content with a link into CamRate.
   I could see autoposting to pintrest, instagram
   - -Also look for platforms where you can easily port content in from
   - -Additionally, look for platforms with flexible API access where you
   can allow users to share their own content to (think IG allows users to
   post to Facebook, Twitter, etc)
   - -Make sharing and redistribution accessible and frictionless to end
   users (easy embed codes, open access apis, etc)
   - -Pull ratings in to the platform of Yelp, Amazon, etc

*Value proposition:* your value is really letting people discover and
archive things they like and dislike. So it would make sense that accessing
this information in aesthetically pleasing ways is probably your early
value proposition to users. Allowing them to create top 25 lists by
categories, bookmark items for christmas lists or wedding registries, could
be useful towards realising the value prop, as well as creating content
they are personally invested in and will share themselves. In general, I
think another large value is the aggregation and comparison of this data
over large swatches of users, with the ability to present that data as
trends


*Optimisation path for all growth hacks*


   - -By segment: certain types of - you want to shift towards targeting
   the most receptive audience segment to increase conversion on growth hacks
   - -By channel: some platforms simply have more arbitrage and flexibility
   than others
   - -By message/copy: most mass outreaches will require slightly varied
   copy to assure not to trigger spam filters


*Marketing infrastructure problems:*

*-SEO infrastructure*


   - -You need a couple of solid press/major site backlinks to really start
   ranking high in google for broad terms, but given your volume of content,
   we can go after niche targeted terms initially
   - -URL directory structure (aka site hierarchy) also makes a huge
   difference here - content should be group in logical structures

*ASO infrastructure*


   - -This is a bit more simple - simple keyword targeting, strategy to
   drive ratings/reviews, backlink strategy. One off implementation with small

*Putting people in an unoptimised funnel/platform without reingagemt
hooks/platform without onboard sandboxing*


   - Simply has lower ROI - catch 22 of early growth
   - less people will make it all the way through down funnel to create
   accounts
   - less people will come back to the platform, and many times you only
   get one shot with some users
   - People need to be driven to points of value and sharing in the
   platform - think LinkedIn's profile completion prompts/mass friend invite
   or twitter on boarding (useronboard.com is a great resource for this)
   and importing contact lists from other platforms to find friends

*Platform access requirements*


   - -to make the most of any web based growth hacking strategy, signups
   need to be allowed through the website. I do not download apps, so
   accessibility and friction reduction to drive early adoption is key,
   particularly if you're looking to drive particular KPIs

*-Content categorisation and presentation*


   - -40 categories is a lot, use a more tiered category structure to allow
   for easier discovery, more granular navigation, etc
   - -Push the most engaging content to high visibility spots to drive
   engagement, then send people to peripheral but related content


*UDID*: 529bf7de8e7bdb2e49987f0c989e560d02bec352

   marketing talent or employees with serious work ethic - seeing a very niche
   senior role asking for 2 years of experience is a major red flag, and makes
   me think it is not really a senior role.
   - I have very broad and extensive experience in a lot of realms of
   marketing (and general business mgmt), including biz dev/b2b, heavy data
   analytics, SEO, and have raised over $600k on crowdfunding platforms
   and large scale seed funding round raises/investor relations campaigns
   ($1million+) in San Francisco. I give talks on growth marketing to MBA
   students at Imperial, KCL, UCL, University of Michigan, Stanford, UC
   Berkeley, etc and have been published for my academic marketing research. I
   currently manage a team of 20 marketers, producers, and events managers for
   one of the largest investment vehicles in terms of portfolio size in the
   world, so I feel this would be a significant step back and into a very
   narrow niche (i.e. referrals), which I don't see as taking advantage of my
   skillset very well (not that I haven't run many referral and evangelist

date: 2016-04-03
to: Michele Parkins <micheleparkins@gmail.com>
subject: Re: URGENT! database error persists
msg_id: 153dccb37857320d
---

Hi Michele,

Given the issues we've encountered, I'm happy to do that. I've also spent
the morning basically teaching myself database management, and looks like
I've set up a solution.

In looking at various error logs, it looks like the issue was something
related to how the theme was storing data - effectively it was storing far
too much and causing it to crash. I've put in a fix in place (I'm actually
pretty impressed with my self I was able to figure it out, although had
some help). However, this also is not an uncommon problem to occur as a
site gets particularly large (which is largely due to images in most cases,
as well as number of visits to your site), and at some point depending on
how you build your site out, you might have to look at simply paying for
more hosting space (another $5 or so per month). In fact, if you expect to
be getting high volume traffic from your upcoming press, you may want to go
ahead and do that.

Re themes: I would recommend picking one from this list:
https://en-gb.wordpress.org/themes/browse/popular/

Popular themes have huge support communities and usually get frequent
updates, which means it's less likely to encounter issues like the one
we're seeing. What you're really looking for is a site where basic page
layout (image size, position) are similar to your existing one, as you will
have to fix anything that isn't. However, I should mention that this is not
a guaranteed fix (nothing with software/web development it) - it is
possible issues may have been transferred from the theme into the database,
although I now also have notifications in place to monitor this as well
should an issue occur again (regardless of whether we switch themes or
not). Worst case scenario, there was even malware in the Kindergarten
theme, at which point there's really not much I can do - I simply cannot be
held responsible for security breaches in a theme picked by a client
developed by a third-party - that would be equivalent to holding a doctor
responsible for common side-effects of a prescription. Although at that
point we could just wipe the server and reupload the content of the site.

If these problems persist into a new theme, it may make sense to hire a
full stack developer for an hour or two to troubleshoot the issue properly.
They would be the person you would have gotten to build a site instead of
me in the first place, and would have charged you about 10x for it, and
likely the same or worse quality aesthetic, as most devs are not designers.
However, for small project based work with a very clear goal, they are
actually a great deal. You could do the same thing with a designer down the
line to get a very polished aesthetic - all at likely a smaller price, as
the initial setup is vague and the stage at which devs usually try to
charge an exorbitant amount of money.

It is very important to note that issues in engineering cannot usually be
solved until they emerge. These crashed have allowed me to put in place
monitoring, which wouldn't have made sense until an issue emerged. It is
simply a catch 22 of developing anything.

I hope this helps, and again, I'm very sorry for the inconvenience. Trouble
shooting a database was certainly not something I had envisioned for this
project, so hopefully installing swap space and a second layer of
additional monitoring fixes the issue, if not changing themes.

Best,

Matthew

---
date: 2016-04-03
to: Michele Parkins <micheleparkins@gmail.com>
subject: Re: URGENT! database error persists
msg_id: 153dbb7d7bbdfa11
---

Hi Michele,

Yes, I received a notification email this morning from the server and reset
it as soon as I woke up.

Unfortunately technology does not always work, and requires a
troubleshooting process with trial and error. I'm sure Kim can tell you a
bit about some of the issues related to Touch Surgery's stability, and that
has a team of 12 developers working on it full time. This is the second
time this issue has emerged (it seems the interval of the issue has
increased dramatically, which is a positive meaning the issue occurs less
often) so I now have another set of information I can use to try and solve
this issue. It's one of the reasons I have an email notification setup for
when the site goes down :)

However, I figure it is useful to have the quick fix for this bug should it
go down again (I am working on a deeper fix):
1. Go to digital ocean and log in
2. Go to you droplet control panel/menu (just click the droplet)
3. Go to the console on your droplet (menu on left side of page)
4. log in (login: root - password: michelewebsite)
5. Type restart, hit enter, and the site should come back up immediately

I must say, I have never encountered this bug personally in 15+ sites I've
built/managed (although it is common and well documented). It is usually
the result of a bad snippet of code, and given that I actually really
didn't code anything on this site, suggests this is likely due to the theme
template, so maybe worth looking for another just in case - actually I
would suggest should the site go down again, we should try a new theme, so
maybe worth picking one out in case this happens again.

I've also pinged a few developers (including the Touch Surgery devs who are
my friends) to ask for some support. Greg Goltsov has been working with me
on this after the last round of bugs, but unfortunately you can't fix
something that isn't broken, and we hoped that our database realignment we
performed when the site went down last time should have fixed everything
(it is the most common resolution to the database error).

You could move to another site, although I would certainly say this is
overkill. Frankly what you really paid me for was linking your DNS, Server,
and Wordpress front end (and SEO and content population, although the
latter is not really skilled work) - that is totally reusable. If anything,
you should just slap a new theme over the existing site, which could
potentially resolve the entire issue (although so could some of the tests I
did this morning) - given the unexpected troubles, I would implement this
for you.

I'm very sorry about the inconvenience, although there is not much I can do
about solving problems until they emerge unfortunately.

Best,

Matthew

to: Michele Parkins <micheleparkins@gmail.com>
subject: Re: update
msg_id: 1536b204c8466637
---

Hi Michele,

Re: the logo. Unfortunately I need to use a square image for the logo in
this template. Can I suggest me cutting out the two flying stars and using
that? Or another option is removing the little man icon all together and
replacing the image on this page with your logo.

Great! One of the reasons why I always recommend WordPress is it's one of
the most accessible platforms to make changes on once you have the initial
templates set up and install done. A quick google search can answer a lot
of questions related to WP (it's estimated up to 1/4 of the internet it
built on it), and I'm always happy to troubleshoot what I can or suggest
solutions. It's also a platform where, if you were to ever want to put a
bit more aesthetic value into the site, there is a huge community of
wordpress developers and designers who could do so for relatively cheap.

Re: ongoing SEO, the one thing that would be incredible to get on now is
just trying to get people (especially the local press you mentioned) to
link back to your site. I'll also create a checklist of more ongoing
activities you can do, including blogging and adding more content to pages
- am in the process of wrapping up an SEO overhaul for another client and
that will be included in their deliverables.

In the meantime, there are 3 realms of SEO: 1) what's in the content of
your pages, 2) what's in the header of your web pages and the structure of
the site, and 3) how other sites interact with yours. I mainly tackled #2,
as #1 is a gradual process heavily reliant on expertise in the form of
writing text to build out new pages on new topics, and #3 is another
gradual process more related to PR that infrastructure or web development.
Both of which are aligned with ongoing activities of promoting your
business, and likely will occur without you even trying by simply having a
webpage now.

All to say, the changes you made with linking won't negatively affect SEO.
In fact, it might even help! I'll explain a bit more in the summary I'll
send along.

Thanks for providing the payment via Venmo.

Please let me know re: the logo, and if there's anything else!

Best,

Matthew

The database error is a widely documented and very vague error that very

know. I'm also running a few tests, so hopefully can identify a root cause.

to: Dean Eisner <dean.eisner@gmail.com>
subject: Consulting Services
msg_id: 153512090e61070c
---

Founder Coaching/General Consulting:

I will provide one-on-one support. This can cover a wide array of topics
from fundraising, marketing, user experience, technical, and more - it is
really up to your discretion. I prefer to be sent a list of 2 or 3 topics
of interest that you are currently focusing on or problems you are facing
with your business a few days before hand so I can provide as much value as
possible.

Brand Consulting:

I will serve as an in-house brand manager. Each week, I will spend an hour
reviewing any new copy and content for release. This requires you to keep
me up to date with any production you are working on via hosting them in
Google folder I will set up so I spend my time reviewing/editing and not
chasing you. This folder will come pre-structured and you will own it, so
it can be used by you as a highly efficient content asset archive to
facilitate access and institutional memory. If you do not have new content
in a given week, I will review old content including website content,
social page information, etc.

Digital Growth Consulting:

We will develop a low-cost, high ROI, multi-channel digital marketing
strategy to grow your business using digital platforms. This can include
email, social media, websites, apps, virtual/augmented reality products,
etc.

ASO/SEO Overhaul:

I will personally update your Search Engine Optimization or App Store
Optimization input settings, site hierarchy, crawl settings, and page
structure to optimize it for organic search, as well as outline solutions
any larger issues I identify. This is only half of the SEO equation, but
the part that you have the ability to immediately influence. I will also
provide a list of activities that fall into your normal business activities
that can performance boost externally controlled SEO factors. Together,
these activities can make orders of magnitude of difference in your organic
visibility.

ASO/SEO Consulting:

I will provide broader ASO/SEO advice, a more suitable option for larger
sites. This can cover SEO strategy, search growth hacking, content
targeting strategy, content optimization, and algorithmic SEO. This will
include 2 one-hour calls, keyword research, and basic analytics tracking
implementation.

Technical Outsourcing Coordinator:

One of the most difficult skills for many non-developers is managing
developers. Without a true understanding of how code works, project/product
management, and the ability to write technical documentation and
specification, it is nearly impossible to manage engineers. You are simply
at their mercy, and have to hope you picked a good freelancer or agency. I
will help you vet suppliers (including one’s from my personal outsourcing
network), structure the terms of your outsourcing contract, and manage the
project to completion. I have experience with C++, Python, PHP, HTML/CSS,
Javascript, JQuery, as well as in managing development of multiple
technical projects ranging from data processing to virtual reality
integrations to software apps.

Business Plan Production:

I will produce a written business plan for you. This includes an executive
summary, business objectives, launch strategy, growth strategy, basic
revenue/cost forecasting,

Basic Pitch Production:

I will develop or create your pitch deck. This includes an original deck
design template, slide design, slide copy writing, basic graphic design,
story development, and 1 session of pitch training. It will include content
about your business model

Advanced Pitch Production:

Basically a super sexy version of Basic Pitch Production

Business Plan & Advanced Pitch Production:

Crowdfunding or Launch Consulting:

I will help guide your product or equity crowdfunding campaign and/or your
public release. This includes platform, reward, analytics, content, press,
influencer, distribution, and conversion strategy. I have raised over
$600,000 in product crowdfunding campaigns, have contacts at Crowdcube and
other equity crowdfunding platforms, and have researched crowdfunding and
PWYW revenue models at UC-Berkeley Haas School of Business. My tactics are
heavily based on academic research I have conducted on influence factors in
crowdfunding raises - this is a topic I will likely pursue a PhD in a
related field to. This includes at least 5 one-hour calls throughout the
course of planning and executing the campaign.

Analytics Consulting: Highly Variable one-time

I will outline the implementation process and end-to-end tracking of
conversion, retention, and virality of your platform so that you can know
exactly how valuable specific users are to your business. With this
knowledge, you can massively decrease costs of acquisition, as well as
optimize your marketing efforts to target and engage your highest value
customers.

Platform Onboard Consulting:

I will help you remove all the friction from your funnel. I’ll go step by
step through your entire onboard process and review it for friction points.
Then we’ll work together to eliminate or reduce those points, as well as to
incorporate behavioral science to increase the number of people who make it
down your funnel. This includes 2 one-hour review calls.

Customer Retention Consulting:

I will develop custom notification, content, and email marketing strategies
designed to increase usage or revenue on your platform. I will also review
your existing platforms for improvements to decrease customer churn. This
includes 3 one-hour review calls.

Promo Video Services:

This can start as low as $1,000 and get larger very quickly depending on
client vision.

Investor Relations and Business Development Consulting:

I will help you develop an investor relations or business development
strategy, as well as a list of contacts. I will template you cold outreach
emails, as well as show you how to track their conversion rates.

Email Automation Consulting and Newsletter Template Production:

I will create an easy to iterate rich email newsletter template, document
protocols for producing email newsletters, and set up Mailchimp account (or
direct you to a service better suited for your needs)

Hi Michele,

I've made the image updates, uploaded your bio photo, and added links to

Re: photos, they're very easy to upload. Just log in, go to the pages
section, and click on the page you want to edit. If you want to add or
remove a header image, go to the featured images area. If you want to add
in the body, just put your cursor where you want the image to go and click
the add media button. To add a link, highlight the text you want and click
the chain link icon.

date: 2016-02-28
to: Hasan Al-Haydar <halhaydar@gmail.com>
subject: amatrixce.com SEO Consultation Proposal
msg_id: 1532a20ef1698df0
---

Hi Hasan,

I've taken a look through everything, and I've found about 200 pieces of
content on your site. However, most are images, which can be optimized
pretty quickly, so I think my £300 cap will be okay, although I can safely
say we're probably going to hit it.

I do want to manage your expectations however. There are two major factors
for ranking in Google search. The first is how well you've set up your page
to be read by Google - that's what I'll be doing for you. The second is how
influential Google thinks your site is. That is accomplished by generating
links back to your site from other sites Google thinks are powerful (i.e.
encyclopedias, university sites, news publications), as well as just the
sheer volume of links back to your site.

I will get the first of these two categories into the best condition it can
be in - this is a one-off thing that really wont need to be done again
unless you're adding new content (and even then it's quite simple).
Specifically I will:

   - Optimize page sizes
   - Kill dead pages and clean sitemaps
   - Install SEO plugins and implement keyword targeting, titles and
   metadescriptions
   - Optimize URLs
   - On-page SEO copywriting optimization
   - Submit robot.txt instructions and sitemaps
   - Geo target your site


As for the second, I'm happy to lay out a roadmap of 10 or 15 things that
you can very easily do to build this - however, this is a gradual process.
Many of the activities that create links back to your site are also ones
that benefit your business (i.e. being quoted in a press article that's
relevant to your business, listing yourself as a business on Google My
Business). I already see some things you could do around the internet that
would immediately create some powerful backlinks for you that you haven't
done.

There are people who will tell you they can sell you backlinks to your site
that will immediately boost you into Google search results. However, this
is against Google's terms of participation in their search engine and will
very quickly get you penalized and blacklisted. What I am proposing is that
I build your SEO infrastructure and additionally can lay out a roadmap to
be able to rank very well in Google that you can easily execute. This will
assure that you will not get penalized and that you wont be affected by
changes in Google's algorithm (which are almost always designed to penalize
people engaging in practices that are violating their terms).

I do have a couple of questions:

   - Do you have Google Analytics
   - Do you have Google Webmaster tools
   - Where do you offer service Geographically
   - Can you make a list of 10 or 15 terms that one of you customers might
   search for if they were looking for your business? Then make a bulleted
   list of 3 more similar terms underneath each one. This is how I will begin
   researching what terms to target for you.


Let me know if this is agreeable to you and we can talk
timeline/payment/admin access so I can get started.

Best,

Matthew

 [image: share on Twitter]

*Growth is a system, not a bag of tricks – Manifest Conference Q&A
video/transcript*
<http://andrewchen.us5.list-manage1.com/track/click?u=96c185f15d9646d8014b765b7&id=bf1957f171&e=a0aa2b77a3>

[image: 2015-10-08 16.16.28][image: 2015-10-08 16.16.20]
I recently was interviewed by Tim Chang
<http://andrewchen.us5.list-manage.com/track/click?u=96c185f15d9646d8014b765b7&id=982ecce1da&e=a0aa2b77a3>,
Managing Director of the Mayfield Fund at the Manifesto conference
<http://andrewchen.us5.list-manage.com/track/click?u=96c185f15d9646d8014b765b7&id=c2b1048a27&e=a0aa2b77a3>.
We talked about growth, what I has learned from trying different tactics,
and how to evaluate the success of growth initiatives. (By the way, SC
Moatti
<http://andrewchen.us5.list-manage.com/track/click?u=96c185f15d9646d8014b765b7&id=c3a93b5fe3&e=a0aa2b77a3>,
the co-producer of Manifesto, also a tech entrepreneur and ex-Facebook PM,
is writing a book on the business mobile called Mobilized
<http://andrewchen.us5.list-manage2.com/track/click?u=96c185f15d9646d8014b765b7&id=9ef87837cb&e=a0aa2b77a3>.
I
had a chance to read it and find her insights really valuable. And the next
Manifesto
<http://andrewchen.us5.list-manage1.com/track/click?u=96c185f15d9646d8014b765b7&id=86c1bf290b&e=a0aa2b77a3>
is dedicated
to mobile.)

You can watch the full video of my talk here
<http://andrewchen.us5.list-manage1.com/track/click?u=96c185f15d9646d8014b765b7&id=5595c9499b&e=a0aa2b77a3>
.

Here’s the key points of the Q&A below. (Thanks to David Grotting
<http://andrewchen.us5.list-manage.com/track/click?u=96c185f15d9646d8014b765b7&id=3714d33298&e=a0aa2b77a3>
for helping with these)

*How Did You Get Started?*

   - Started in Venture Capital as an entrepreneur in residence at Mohr
   Davidow Ventures.
   - One of my most important experiences was working in Ad Tech
      - You spend all of your time thinking about quantitative customer
      acquisition for tens of thousands of customers.
      - You learn all the interesting nuances of different business models
      and gain a keen sense of customer funnel optimization and key
metrics like
      cost per customer and LTV.
      - One example being working with a dating site and realizing that the
      average time for a dating “match” was about 4 months so it’s important to
      get users to sign up for a 12 month subscription. This is very different
      than a gaming company strategy, as a contrast.
      - I was one of the few people who had all this quantitative
      experience with customer acquisition and wanted to apply it in a consumer
      context.


   - At this time in ‘07 the IQ around consumer products was was relatively
   low – and investors were making investments off number of hundreds of
   thousands of registered users. It’s been amazing to see over the the last
   couple years how much the industry has upgraded its thinking.

*Lessons To Share About Growth:*

   - Growth is not a bunch of small, tactical growth hacks. (Make a button
   this color, etc.)
   - Growth is a full model and system with linked parts and loops that
   align with your business
   - Tactics can be used to optimize loops, but the entire model must be
   well understood first.
   - If you’re going to focus on virality – it’s not about just building
   something cool, but actually thinking how one batch of users end up
   inviting the next batch of users and optimizing that entire loop with with
   tactics.
   - You must put in the hard work to build a framework that is
   situationally right for your product.

*What is a Growth Hacker?*

   - Sean Ellis coined the term while working with Sequoia companies. It
   was the embodiment of a direct response marketer combined with a product
   manager that had a deep focus on analytics.
   - Growth is fundamentally a product thing: Requires true team effort of
   PMs, designers, developers, etc. that utilize software to drive KPIs
   - Growth Hacking has started to become a negative signal: Next
   generation of consultant keyword/title

*Metrics should be a reflection of the strategy you’ve decided*

   - Be careful about focusing on vanity metrics like daily installs
   - Churn is one of the most defining aspects of whether or not you have a
   sustainable business.
   - Have your metrics prove that you are creating a sustainable growth
   model
   - In the beginning, entrepreneurs build a product from the heart and
   have the ability to be hyperattentive, listen to each customer, and get all
   the details right. You then get to a point where there is a phase
   transition where you have to truly scale, and that tends to be the most
   difficult.
   - Finding product/market fit is key before scaling growth efforts
   - Mobile is in a dark time and it is very difficult to grow a mobile app
   now. It is daunting for new startups as successful apps are prioritized in
   rankings and it becomes more difficult to gain new-app visibility. You must
   continue to look for new platforms.

*Messaging apps are going to create the next platform beyond app stores*

   - Messaging is where social was in ‘07/’08
   - Just like adding social to other categories of products has been
   successful (Social Reviews = Yelp, Social Videos = YouTube, etc.),
   messaging will have opportunities to be paired with other categories of
   products with success.
   - Messaging and communication is the killer app for your phone.
   - I’m hopeful that messaging will create the next generation platform
   for mobile app distribution.
   - Working backwards when you have a new idea or new product and thinking
   about how it relates to messaging is a very important question to ask if
   you want to be hitting scale 2-3 years from now.

*Who are your influencers and what are some of your favorite books?*

   - Book: My Life in Advertising
   <http://andrewchen.us5.list-manage.com/track/click?u=96c185f15d9646d8014b765b7&id=7173d4b8a0&e=a0aa2b77a3>
   - Stratechery
   <http://andrewchen.us5.list-manage.com/track/click?u=96c185f15d9646d8014b765b7&id=d253b3047f&e=a0aa2b77a3>:
   Ben Thompson
   - Ben Evans
   <http://andrewchen.us5.list-manage.com/track/click?u=96c185f15d9646d8014b765b7&id=2654001319&e=a0aa2b77a3>
   at a16z
   - Book: Designing Interactions
   <http://andrewchen.us5.list-manage1.com/track/click?u=96c185f15d9646d8014b765b7&id=829a6b9a4a&e=a0aa2b77a3>
   - More tech books
   <http://andrewchen.us5.list-manage2.com/track/click?u=96c185f15d9646d8014b765b7&id=e52a91b26c&e=a0aa2b77a3>

date: 2016-02-06
to: Michele Parkins <micheleparkins@gmail.com>
subject: Re: creating a new website...help!
msg_id: 152b8b60e0d655ce
---

Yup - just pick a template and list out the pages you'd imagine having on
your website! I should note, there are also paid templates, but I imagine
you'll find a good one for free.

There are also a few quick things we'll have to do with accounts,
specifically: I'll need access for about 2 days to the account where you
bought your domain name; I'll create you an account on a hosting platform
that you'll need to plug in payment info on and then takeover/change
passwords; I'll create your wordpress account and get everything set up.

Once we get all that out of the way, I can let you know how long it will
take and how much I'd charge - I don't imagine it would be anything to
costly - $750 at most and as little as $300 - possibly even cheaper.

I should mention, the template itself will probably not be EXACTLY what you
envision - there will probably be a few quirks and thing you'd like
removed. I can definitely make a few of the simpler changes, but that's not
my strong suit - I just mention this to bear in mind that more complicated
aesthetic changes could be a bit out of my range, but are generally quite
easy to make happen with an hourly freelance wordpress developer.

Hope this answers all your questions!

Best,

Matthew

From: megan@startupbootcamp.org
To: davetompkins@hotmail.com

Hi Dave,

I hope this email finds you well and thank you for volunteering to join us
as a mentor at our upcoming FastTrack event in Atlanta!

We'd like to continue actively promoting the event on social media and were
hoping you could send out a tweet and/or LinkedIn update encouraging
startups to apply to pitch.  I have included a sample tweet below:

 " #ATL <https://twitter.com/hashtag/ATL?src=hash> #FinTech
<https://twitter.com/hashtag/FinTech?src=hash> #Startups
<https://twitter.com/hashtag/Startups?src=hash> apply for the #SBCFastTrack
<https://twitter.com/hashtag/SBCFastTrack?src=hash> @EmoryGoizueta
<https://twitter.com/EmoryGoizueta> and be the next cohort! http://
sta.cr/2dkg1  <https://t.co/LEK5uXbzaD>   "

As a reminder, the event will take place this Friday, February 5th, and
will consist of two sessions (morning and afternoon -- timings have been
detailed below).  If you can no longer attend the session(s) you signed up
for, please let me know.

*What does being a mentor involve?*
Each session involves 5 startups pitching for 5 minutes (different startups
at each session).  After the 5 pitches are complete we will break the
mentors up into small groups where they will meet with each of the startups
who pitched (speed dating style where the groups of mentors stay seated and
the startups move from group to group) for 10-15 minute feedback sessions.
The feedback is informal and can cover anything from the startup's business
model, pitch style, customer acquisition, etc.

Our mentors come from a wide range of backgrounds (bankers, VCs,
entrepreneurs, technology and innovation professionals, etc.) and are a
tremendous resource for startups who pitch at the event.


*Where is the location?*
Goizueta Business School, Room 338 (East Wing)
Emory University
1300 Clifton Rd NE
Atlanta, GA 30322

*What is the schedule?*
We ask that you arrive 15 minutes before your session (morning or
afternoon) begins.  You will find the session timing details below.  You
are, of course, also welcome to join us for lunch.

Morning Session
09:30 - 09:45 Introduction
09:45 - 10:15 Team 1-5 pitches
10:15 - 12:00 Team 1-5 mentorship

Lunch
12:00 - 12:45

Afternoon Session
13:00 - 13:15 Introduction
13:15 - 13:45 Team 6-10 pitches
13:45 - 15:15 Team 6-10 mentorship

Also, if you feel that anyone in your network would be a great addition as
a mentor at the event, please send them the following google form to
complete and we will be in touch with more details:
http://goo.gl/forms/7BvivG7LPw

Thank you for your help and I look forward to seeing you this Friday!

Best,

Megan

date: 2016-02-05
to: Michele Parkins <micheleparkins@gmail.com>
subject: Re: creating a new website...help!
msg_id: 152b1f61537394d5
---

Hi Michele,

Awww, tell Tyler I said hi! I was actually awake although was exhausted
from 2 of the craziest weeks of my life, so wanted to read your message in
the morning when I could answer coherently- sorry to disappoint there :)

re: website - I'd say if it's something not too complex, you could be fine
building it with pretty minimal development. There is a bit of technical
know-how involved with the initial setup, but I can do that for you pretty
quickly (definitely don't do the initial setup on your own - buying a
domain name is simple but after that it gets quite complicated). I would
say the best starting point is can you provide an outline of the pages of
the site and the sort of content you envision on them?

The next step would then be going here and picking a theme that you like
the aesthetic of that would fit the images and text you envision well
(keeping in mind colour and images are very easy to change, but page layout
and structure is quite difficult):
https://wordpress.org/themes/search/care/ (care
is just a random search term i picked that returned some good results, but
dig around or just google "free wordpress themes therapist" or terms like
that til you find a template you like).

If your site is simple enough in terms of content and functionality, I
think it should be easy enough for me to set up the framework for you and
let you edit as you see fit (but can help if you have any difficulties - in
general wordpress is a very user friendly platform). Then at the end I can
do a quick SEO crack through at the end. You could also probably find a
tech savvy kid to do the nitty gritty work in terms of populating
content/text to the site.

I definitely do think a website will dramatically increase the inbound
interest you see from potential clients (especially as more and more
millennial become parents). A website is basically the cornerstone of your
digital presence, and while very simple, a wordpress site is a great
starting point. The next step after a website would be looking into email
marketing.

Hope all is well, and please give Kim my best!

Matthew

date: 2016-02-01
to: Kevin Darcy <kevin@mytutorweb.co.uk>
subject: Following up from last week
msg_id: 1529dae98ceeb22f
---

Hey Kevin,

Was lovely to meet you last week. I did have a bit of an epiphany in terms
of the general communication tactics/messaging that might be useful.

Basically, figure out how to tap into nerd culture. I kind of grew up on
the verge of when it became cool, but people still made fun of geeks when I
was a kid. Towards the end of my unim it started to become cool to be
smart, and then with the whole tech startup boom, it's sort of been fully
embraced.

Anyways, try and figure out how to communicate nerd-cool in a way that
doesn't turn off kids, and that might really make your messaging click. I
would also recommend focus grouping your target audience (students) and
ask, as well as run them through executions for feedback. If kids think
it's cool to be a nerd/smart it could be a great messaging technique, or
maybe you'll see that it's only in older groups where the stigma of
nerdiness has died (i.e. my assumptions could be totally wrong, so I would
suggest verifying them, as with any assumption).

This was the deck on growth hacking I mentioned that I would include - the
tactics aren't right for every company, but it does a good job explaining
the general digital arbitrage hunting mentality, and has some great
immediately actionable tools:
http://www.slideshare.net/MarcusMatthewCurran/how-to-attract-humans-vincent-dignan

Also, this was the education accelerator in London that my friends runs -
happy to make an intro: http://emerge.education/

Let me know if there's anything I'm missing, or if you have any questions I
can help with!

Best,

Matthew

date: 2016-01-29
to: Andy Shannon <andy@startupbootcamp.org>
subject: Re: Your UK Startup Accelerators, Contests & Funds Jan 28 - Feb 4
msg_id: 1528d8e4917be1ba
---

Thanks for mapping all this out the logic.

To respond to the issues you raised that programs had with the original
consolidated FastTrack - 1) I see this being the true pain point, although
I think a ranking system (rank the accelerators you want to be in from most
to least desirable) could solve this once we're fully on Salesforce. 2) we
should be able to address this with conditional survey logic, although not
sure how much f6s allows for out-of-the-box. 3) This actually is my biggest
pro for separate applications - it's great from a longtail SEO standpoint,
and allows for programs to provide a lot more detail (although I'm not sure
if the latter would actually benefit or hinder our "conversions" compared
to a consolidated UX).

Basically to say that there are certainly pros and cons to each, and I
can't say - but I do think the organic visibility of being "super popular"
is valuable. Long run, I think it would be great to host our FastTrack
applications both on f6s and getfeedback, but that's too resource intensive
right now.

I'm going to be making a list of all of these sorts of ideas/projects. Any
changes we can make to the underlying application funnel will amplify our
outbound marketing efforts though, which is why I want to make sure we do
take on some of these more infrastructure related tasks - the ease and
benefits of scaling good mkt infrastructure are pretty dramatic compared to
bad :).

---
date: 2016-01-28
to: Andy Shannon <andy@startupbootcamp.org>
subject: Fwd: Your UK Startup Accelerators, Contests & Funds Jan 28 - Feb 4
msg_id: 1528a1d2f9724963
---

So I've been thinking on this for a while - TechStars has a great growth
hack on f6s that might be smart to replicate.

They consolidate their applications so they're always running from the same
application page. I.E. it says they've seen like 20k submissions of
applications for their programs, thus making sure they're always the most
popular app on the platform (a prominent sorting feature, but that being
said, our fasttracks and then some of our programs are close seconds). this
means their links never break, and that that their application page likely
has very strong SEO due to inbound. It creates a very streamlined UX, which
is important for driving people down a funnel. This also means their
application link gets served out in more city newsletters (e.g. I receive a
newsletter for London accelerators receiving apps - we weren't on the last
one because we're not accepting apps. TechStars London was on it, but so
was Atlanta and Boulder, because it's all just one app, but the cities that
are currently accepting are listed individually).

I know there is an organizational barrier for us doing something like that,
but I could see changes along these lines having a pretty strong effect if
we can manage the issues it might raise around lead follow up (how do we
handle teams applying to multiple programs, etc.). Maybe its just having a
general application always up so we can add interested teams to our
databases for Francisco to draw from for sourcing, or at the very least
just so we can let them know when programs are open via email blast.

This isn't really even on my radar right now, I just wanted to raise the
point while I have it clearly conceptualized in my mind from seeing the F6S
newsletter.

to: "Jeffrey Martín" <jeffrey@honorcodeatl.org>
subject: Re: idan beck
msg_id: 15240f29c005f542
---

Basically the way to summarize:

-Typically when people are in prototyping phase, theyre experimenting with
different structures, reworking the code, optimizing functions, etc.

-Idan doesn't do that (see his response to when I ask him what his first
hack was). He doesn't prototype. He maps out a system top to bottom and
then implements it. I.E. everything is deliberate (sort of Randian theory
of art applied to CS if you will). He's been coding since he was about 5.

Dylan will also get a big kick out of the fact that Idan built a web based
collaborative DAW with virtually no latency (think Google Docs X Ableton
Live)

date: 2016-01-13
to: ttownley@zaxbys.com
subject: Re: Introduction / Zaxby's Growth
msg_id: 1523b69db03b928e
---

Thanks Melissa,

Hi Tom!

As Melissa mentioned, I've been quite missing a certain chicken franchise
since I moved to London. Actually, back in college at Michigan, my friends
who grew up in various southern states and I used to drive to Ohio just to
pick up catering orders of nuggets and sandwiches. I always used to
half-joke that I would have loved to work in Chick-fil-a's marketing
department (they really do have some fantastic campaigns), except for the
fact that I could never work at a company so ethically challenged.

If you're ever opening a Zaxby's in the UK, please do let me know! Fried
Chicken in general a huge phenomena here, and most are truly awful. "PFC"s
(Perfect Fried Chickens) are everywhere - effectively HORRIBLE KFC
knockoffs, often with hilariously ripped names meant to make them seem as
American as possible (Tennessee Fried Chicken, Kentucky Chicken Fry, etc.).
Chicken frys, as they're called, also are often used as a metric (in
comparison with coffee shops in a given area) to calculate gentrification
here
<http://t.sidekickopen35.com/e1t/c/5/f18dQhb0S7lC8dDMPbW2n0x6l2B9nMJN7t5XZsQsBhjW1qMyFK5wvHZnVRJgRK56dP4Wf34C7ZF02?t=https%3A%2F%2Fmedium.com%2F%40Sam_Floy%2Fhow-to-know-if-where-you-live-is-up-and-coming-fried-chicken-vs-coffee-shops-546080119f98%23.6xr751jv6&si=5804247449337856&pi=f7363424-4659-4026-f2be-cd0b039c05ff>
.

I'm sure you're aware, but the most successful franchise in the space here
is Nando's. A similar sort of cultish brand equity as Chick-fil-a or
Zaxby's, and there's a whole viral WOM movement around "cheeky Nandos".
Happy to chat sometime and discuss what the market looks like here or
anything about facilitating digital/viral growth. I mainly do digital
marketing infrastructure and growth hacking consulting for tech startups,
but it's often quite applicable and significantly more effective when
employed by an organization that has bandwidth to execute more effectively.

Best,

Matthew

date: 2016-01-13
to: Jan Matern <jan@emergeventurelab.com>
subject: Re: Favour?
msg_id: 1523b093efad131a
---

Hi Jan,

Sorry for the delay on this - there were a few people at Startupbootcamp
that were interested, but we're prepping to launch a few new programs, so
no one has the bandwidth right now unfortunately. Most of them try to
maintain a semblance of a work life balance, whereas I don't really :).
However, there are a few people I think might be a good fit in the future
with a bit more notice, and I'd be happy to intro you (or potentially serve
as an advisor myself).

I conceivably would be interested in investing as well, although would be
very picky. I also could certainly feed interesting companies to the
corporate VCs we partner with for sourcing activities.

In terms of marketplace/mobile, I have quite a bit of experience with that.

   - Incident Technologies had an in app store to purchase songs (that you
   would subsequently learn how to play on our hardware) - we signed licensing
   agreements with Sony/ATV, Warner Music, and EMI, including for the full
   Beatles catalogue.
   - Hackster.io is more of a hardware community platform than a
   marketplace, but does have an integration to pull in shopping info from
   various sites so people can buy components to the projects they're looking
   at and build them themselves
   - Touch Surgery was a mobile-only surgical education platform, with
   effectively the equivalent of an in app store, except all the content was
   free (for now). We worked with Stanford, Yale, Oxford, UPenn, Harvard, etc
   to find people to publish the content on our platform, and had about 600k
   users when I left. I launched our curriculums into Stanford, UPenn, and
   John Hopkins and managed our relationships with our authors (generally
   chairs of various surgical departments in the medical schools) and users
   there.
   - I do a lot of ASO consulting (SEO for app stores). I've seen a
   company's download rate go from 500 to 5000 per day simply by fixing their
   event listing, so potentially a very high impact solution for many mobile
   companies

I actually very vividly remember us having a conversation after my little
mock-interview about how I completely glossed over the content curation
aspect of the company I was talking to. I guess to me, that's because
content is so primary that it's the last thing I really address, as it's so
easy to fix for most organisations. However, it's certainly been eye
opening to see the lack of attention that gets paid to content as well as
marketing in general in European ecosystems, even within content-driven
startups.

I'm actually grabbing lunch with Lucy in a few minutes, but let me know if
you might want to grab a drink in the coming weeks and catch up - I'm
traveling quite a lot, but maybe after the panel at Startup Europe Week.

Best,

Matthew

to: Idan Beck <idanbeck@gmail.com>
subject: Friends visitng SF 2/9-2/21
msg_id: 15238094ff4ac6b4
---

Hey Idan,

Hope all is well and you're off to a lovely new year!

Two of my closest childhood friends recently launched a startup building
social impact oriented STEM education programs (particularly for school
districts with underserved female and minority groups), and will be
visiting SF to meet with various potential investors and mentors.

I've known both founders since elementary or middle school - one was
probably my best friend growing up (likely still to this day) and just
completed a masters in educational psychology research before moving to
this. We actually taught each other how to play guitar and used to read the
DSM-IV together as kids.

The other was also a very close friend and possibly the most inspiring
success-against-the-odds story I know (born into an unfathomably destitute
home in innercity Atlanta, came to our private school on a full ride
scholarship, then Penn Wharton on a full ride, then Goldman Sachs where he
hated it, and then did an education post-grad at Brown while teaching and
consulting for TFA and learning front end development). He's done a really
impressive job laying the foundations for their company, but I think could
really use some guidance as they start the push to bring it to fruition.

I was wondering if you might be willing to let them buy you a drink or
dinner and chat with them a little. They're both new to startups but
extremely driven, and I think that you could provide incredibly valuable
insight to them in terms of how they invest their time in developing their
platform and developing something that will actually... work. I'd love to

date: 2016-01-05
to: Nikita Korotaev <nikita@glocalpartners.com>
subject: image-to-text ratio info
msg_id: 152140dfc3057b0e
---

Salesforce: "Too many images (or too large of an image) compared to text in
an HTML email can be considered spammy. Adding more text and/or reducing
the number and size of images may help. Keep in mind that lots of email
clients block images by default, so there's a good chance that even if your
image-heavy emails make it into the inbox, your recipients don't see the
images automatically. Also, make sure your images include alt tags."

Mailchimp Users' Most Common Errors (and frequency):
BODY: HTML has a low ratio of text to image area    (1,217)
BODY: Message only has text/html MIME parts    (971)
BODY: HTML has a low ratio of text to image area    (729)
BODY: HTML and text parts are different    (625)
SUBJECT: Subject is all capitals    (324)
BODY: HTML and text parts are different    (279)
BODY: HTML: images with 2400-2800 bytes of words    (211)
BODY: HTML: images with 2000-2400 bytes of words    (194)
BODY: HTML: images with 1200-1600 bytes of words    (178)
BODY: HTML: images with 1600-2000 bytes of words    (178)

Pretty solid summary of Spam Assassin filters (commonly run on enterprise
servers) by Pure360, an email provider we used at Touch Surgery. Heinous
support but good functionality:
http://www.pure360.com/why-is-image-to-text-ratio-so-important/

I also found a blog that completely contradicts image to text ratios as a
spam factor here, although there are a number of potentially confounding
uncontrolled variables:
https://www.emailonacid.com/blog/article/email-development/does_text_to_image_ratio_affect_deliverability

This is also a solid summary on building email sender reputation:
http://help.infusionsoft.com/userguides/campaigns-and-broadcasts/email-deliverability-guide/10-steps-to-build-trust-as-an-email-sender

Ultimately, I think if you have the bandwidth, a/b testing is always safer.
If not, the <40% image / >60% text in html is the way to go.

Hey Matt,

That's fine, and I appreciate the kind words. I'm going to talk to a few
mentors, sleep on it, and will let you know my course of action tomorrow.
However, a few of my mentors raised their eyebrows when I mentioned I would
be working on this project with Startup Europe, and I think I understand
why now...

The lack of organization by Startup Europe has cost me a significant amount
of my time in backtracking to delete marketing best practices I've
implemented in order to replace them with lesser alternatives. It would
have been very easily prevented through Startup Europe having the slightest
bit of respect for their organizers to recognize that as we are donating
our time to them, the least they can do is not waste it by putting in an
hour of work to set up protocol ahead of time. However, to me it seems like
the main goal of the marketing of SEW is to push XING (an older and far
lesser platform to eventbrite that was created by an advisor of Startup
Europe), which does not align with my goals of bettering myself and putting
on a good event. I also find it highly manipulative the way they did this
under the guise of it being a partnership.

Ironic, but to me this really sums up the difference between SF and EU
startup ecosystems and highlights the difference between a knowledge
economy/meritocracy/work ethic and... not... Certainly a valuable
educational experience though!

Whatever I decide, It's been an absolute pleasure getting to know you
better and working with Sheng, Ellenie, and yourself - I hope I have the
opportunity again in the future.

Best,

Matthew
